911

912

913 <section id="_1">

914

915 <h2>

916General Information About Melanoma</h2>

917

918 <div id="_section_1" class="pdq-sections">

919<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

920<h6>

921In This Section</h6>

922<ul>

923<li>

924<a href="#_5_toc">

925Incidence and Mortality</a>

926</li>

927<li>

928<a href="#_661_toc">

929Risk Factors</a>

930</li>

931<li>

932<a href="#_8_toc">

933Anatomy</a>

934</li>

935<li>

936<a href="#_387_toc">

937Screening </a>

938</li>

939<li>

940<a href="#_17_toc">

941Clinical Features</a>

942</li>

943<li>

944<a href="#_22_toc">

945Diagnosis</a>

946</li>

947<li>

948<a href="#_25_toc">

949Prognostic Factors</a>

950</li>

951</ul>

952</nav>

953<div class="pdq-hp-patient-toggle">

954<a href="/types/skin/patient/melanoma-treatment-pdq">

955Go to Patient Version</a>

956</div>

957<p id="_593" tabindex="-1">

958Melanoma is a malignant tumor of melanocytes, which are the cells that make the pigment melanin and are derived from the neural crest. Although most melanomas arise in the skin, they may also arise from mucosal surfaces or at other sites to which neural crest cells migrate, including the uveal tract. Uveal melanomas differ significantly from cutaneous melanoma in incidence, prognostic factors, molecular characteristics, and treatment. For more information, see <a href="/types/eye/hp/intraocular-melanoma-treatment-pdq">

959Intraocular (Uveal) Melanoma Treatment</a>

960.</p>

961<section id="_5">

962<h3 id="_5_toc">

963Incidence and Mortality</h3>

964<p id="_6" tabindex="-1">

965Estimated new cases and deaths from melanoma in the United States in 2023:[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

9661</a>

967]</p>

968<div class="pdq-content-list">

969<ul id="_7">

970<li>

971New cases: 97,610.</li>

972<li>

973Deaths: 7,990.</li>

974</ul>

975</div>

976<p id="_750" tabindex="-1">

977Skin cancer is the most common malignancy diagnosed in the United States, and invasive melanoma represents about 1% of skin cancers but results in most deaths.[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

9781</a>

979,<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

9802</a>

981] Since the early 2000s, the incidence of melanoma in people younger than 50 years declined by about 1% per year in men and stabilized in women. From 2015 to 2019, the incidence in people aged 50 years and older stabilized in men and increased by about 1% per year in women.[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

9821</a>

983] Older men are at highest risk; however, melanoma is the most common cancer in young adults aged 25 to 29 years and the second most common cancer in those aged 15 to 29 years.[<a href="#cit/section_1.3">

9843</a>

985] Ocular melanoma is the most common cancer of the eye, with approximately 2,000 cases diagnosed annually.</p>

986</section>

987<section id="_661">

988<h3 id="_661_toc">

989Risk Factors</h3>

990<p id="_662" tabindex="-1">

991Risk factors for melanoma include both intrinsic (genetic and phenotype) and extrinsic (environmental or exposure) factors:</p>

992<div class="pdq-content-list">

993<ul id="_663">

994<li>

995 Sun exposure.</li>

996<li>

997Pigmentary characteristics.</li>

998<li>

999Multiple nevi.</li>

1000<li>

1001Family and personal history of melanoma.</li>

1002<li>

1003 Immunosuppression.</li>

1004<li>

1005Environmental exposures.</li>

1006</ul>

1007</div>

1008<p id="_664" tabindex="-1">

1009For more information about risk factors, see <a href="/types/skin/hp/skin-prevention-pdq#_146">

1010Skin Cancer Prevention</a>

1011 and <a href="/types/skin/hp/skin-genetics-pdq#_683">

1012Genetics of Skin Cancer</a>

1013.</p>

1014</section>

1015<section id="_8">

1016<h3 id="_8_toc">

1017Anatomy</h3>

1018<p id="_986" tabindex="-1">

1019<figure id="figure_343" class="image-center-medium">

1020<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/624959.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1021Enlarge</a>

1022<img id="_343" alt="Schematic representation of normal skin; drawing shows normal skin anatomy, including the epidermis, dermis, hair follicles, sweat glands, hair shafts, veins, arteries, fatty tissue, nerves, lymph vessels, oil glands, and subcutaneous tissue. The pullout shows a close-up of the squamous cell and basal cell layers of the epidermis, the basement membrane in between the epidermis and dermis, and the dermis with blood vessels. Melanin is shown in the cells. A melanocyte is shown in the layer of basal cells at the deepest part of the epidermis." title="Schematic representation of normal skin; drawing shows normal skin anatomy, including the epidermis, dermis, hair follicles, sweat glands, hair shafts, veins, arteries, fatty tissue, nerves, lymph vessels, oil glands, and subcutaneous tissue. The pullout shows a close-up of the squamous cell and basal cell layers of the epidermis, the basement membrane in between the epidermis and dermis, and the dermis with blood vessels. Melanin is shown in the cells. A melanocyte is shown in the layer of basal cells at the deepest part of the epidermis." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/624959-750.jpg">

1023<figcaption class="caption-container">

1024Schematic representation of normal skin. Melanocytes are also present in normal skin and serve as the source cell for melanoma. The relatively avascular epidermis houses both basal cell keratinocytes and squamous epithelial keratinocytes, the source cells for basal cell carcinoma and squamous cell carcinoma, respectively. The separation between epidermis and dermis occurs at the basement membrane zone, located just inferior to the basal cell keratinocytes.</figcaption>

1025</figure>

1026</p>

1027</section>

1028<section id="_387">

1029<h3 id="_387_toc">

1030Screening </h3>

1031<p id="_397" tabindex="-1">

1032For more information, see <a href="/types/skin/hp/skin-screening-pdq">

1033Skin Cancer Screening</a>

1034.</p>

1035</section>

1036<section id="_17">

1037<h3 id="_17_toc">

1038Clinical Features</h3>

1039<p id="_18" tabindex="-1">

1040Melanoma occurs predominantly in adults, and more than 50% of the cases arise in apparently normal areas of the skin. Although melanoma can occur anywhere, including on mucosal surfaces and the uvea, in women it occurs more commonly on the extremities, and in men it occurs most commonly on the trunk or head and neck.[<a href="#cit/section_1.4">

10414</a>

1042]</p>

1043<p id="_505" tabindex="-1">

1044Early signs in a nevus that would suggest a malignant change include the following:</p>

1045<div class="pdq-content-list">

1046<ul id="_506">

1047<li>

1048Darker or variable discoloration.</li>

1049<li>

1050Itching.</li>

1051<li>

1052 An increase in size or the development of satellites.</li>

1053<li>

1054Ulceration or bleeding (later signs).</li>

1055</ul>

1056</div>

1057<figure id="figure_941" class="image-center">

1058<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/765750.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1059Enlarge</a>

1060<img id="_941" alt="Photographs showing a large, asymmetrical, red and brown lesion on the skin (panel 1); a brown lesion with a large and irregular border on the skin (panel 2); and a large, asymmetrical, scaly, red and brown lesion on the skin (panel 3)." title="Photographs showing a large, asymmetrical, red and brown lesion on the skin (panel 1); a brown lesion with a large and irregular border on the skin (panel 2); and a large, asymmetrical, scaly, red and brown lesion on the skin (panel 3)." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/765750-750.jpg">

1061<figcaption class="caption-container">

1062Melanomas with characteristic asymmetry, border irregularity, color variation, and large diameter.</figcaption>

1063</figure>

1064</section>

1065<section id="_22">

1066<h3 id="_22_toc">

1067Diagnosis</h3>

1068<p id="_389" tabindex="-1">

1069A biopsy, preferably by local excision, should be performed for any suspicious lesions. Suspicious lesions should never be shaved off or cauterized. An experienced pathologist should examine the specimens to allow for microstaging.</p>

1070<p id="_507" tabindex="-1">

1071Studies show that distinguishing between benign pigmented lesions and early melanomas can be difficult, and even experienced dermatopathologists can have differing opinions. To reduce the possibility of misdiagnosis for an individual patient, a second review by an independent qualified pathologist should be considered.[<a href="#cit/section_1.5">

10725</a>

1073,<a href="#cit/section_1.6">

10746</a>

1075] Agreement between pathologists in the histological diagnosis of melanomas and benign pigmented lesions has been found to be considerably variable.[<a href="#cit/section_1.5">

10765</a>

1077,<a href="#cit/section_1.6">

10786</a>

1079]</p>

1080<p id="_508" tabindex="-1">

1081Evidence (discordance in histological evaluation):</p>

1082<div class="pdq-content-list">

1083<ol id="_509">

1084<li>

1085One study found that there was discordance in the diagnosis of melanoma versus benign lesions in 37 of 140 cases examined by a panel of experienced dermatopathologists. For the histological classification of cutaneous melanoma, the highest concordance was attained for Breslow thickness and presence of ulceration, while the agreement was poor for other histological features such as Clark level of invasion, presence of regression, and lymphocytic infiltration.[<a href="#cit/section_1.5">

10865</a>

1087]</li>

1088<li>

1089In another study, 38% of cases examined by a panel of expert pathologists had two or more discordant interpretations.[<a href="#cit/section_1.6">

10906</a>

1091]</li>

1092</ol>

1093</div>

1094</section>

1095<section id="_25">

1096<h3 id="_25_toc">

1097Prognostic Factors</h3>

1098<p id="_235" tabindex="-1">

1099Prognosis is affected by the characteristics of primary and metastatic tumors. The most important prognostic factors have been incorporated into the revised 2009 American Joint Committee on Cancer staging and include the following:[<a href="#cit/section_1.4">

11004</a>

1101,<a href="#cit/section_1.7">

11027</a>

1103-<a href="#cit/section_1.9">

11049</a>

1105]</p>

1106<div class="pdq-content-list">

1107<ul id="_511">

1108<li>

1109Thickness and/or level of invasion of the melanoma.</li>

1110<li>

1111Mitotic index, defined as mitoses per millimeter.</li>

1112<li>

1113Ulceration or bleeding at the primary site.</li>

1114<li>

1115Number of regional lymph nodes involved, with distinction of macrometastasis and micrometastasis.</li>

1116<li>

1117Systemic metastasis.<div class="pdq-content-list">

1118<ul id="_751" class="list-dash">

1119<li>

1120Site&#8212;nonvisceral versus lung versus all other visceral sites.</li>

1121<li>

1122Elevated serum lactate dehydrogenase level.</li>

1123</ul>

1124</div>

1125</li>

1126</ul>

1127</div>

1128<p id="_513" tabindex="-1">

1129Patients who are younger, who are female, and who have melanomas on their extremities generally have better prognoses.[<a href="#cit/section_1.4">

11304</a>

1131,<a href="#cit/section_1.7">

11327</a>

1133-<a href="#cit/section_1.9">

11349</a>

1135]</p>

1136<p id="_558" tabindex="-1">

1137Microscopic satellites, recorded as present or absent, in stage I melanoma may be a poor prognostic histological factor, but this is controversial.[<a href="#cit/section_1.10">

113810</a>

1139] The presence of tumor infiltrating lymphocytes, which may be categorized as brisk, nonbrisk, or absent, is under study as a potential prognostic factor.[<a href="#cit/section_1.11">

114011</a>

1141]</p>

1142<p id="_390" tabindex="-1">

1143The risk of relapse decreases substantially over time, although late relapses are not uncommon.[<a href="#cit/section_1.12">

114412</a>

1145,<a href="#cit/section_1.13">

114613</a>

1147] </p>

1148</section>

1209 <section id="_883">

1210

1211 <h2>

1212Cellular and Molecular Classification of Melanoma</h2>

1213

1214 <div id="_section_883" class="pdq-sections">

1215<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

1216<h6>

1217In This Section</h6>

1218<ul>

1219<li>

1220<a href="#_1088_toc">

1221Genomic Classification<ul>

1222<li>

1223<a href="#_1089_toc">

1224Cutaneous melanoma</a>

1225</li>

1226<li>

1227<a href="#_1096_toc">

1228Uveal melanoma</a>

1229</li>

1230</ul>

1231</a>

1232</li>

1233</ul>

1234</nav>

1235<p id="_32" tabindex="-1">

1236The descriptive terms for clinicopathological cellular subtypes of malignant melanoma should be considered of historic interest only; they do not have independent prognostic or therapeutic significance. The cellular subtypes are the following:</p>

1237<div class="pdq-content-list">

1238<ul id="_35">

1239<li>

1240Superficial spreading.

1241</li>

1242<li>

1243Nodular.</li>

1244<li>

1245Lentigo maligna.</li>

1246<li>

1247Acral lentiginous (palmar/plantar and subungual).</li>

1248<li>

1249Miscellaneous unusual types:<div class="pdq-content-list">

1250<ul id="_257" class="list-dash">

1251<li>

1252Mucosal lentiginous (oral and genital).</li>

1253<li>

1254Desmoplastic.</li>

1255<li>

1256Verrucous.</li>

1257</ul>

1258</div>

1259</li>

1260</ul>

1261</div>

1262<section id="_1088">

1263<h3 id="_1088_toc">

1264Genomic Classification</h3>

1265<section id="_1089">

1266<h4 id="_1089_toc">

1267Cutaneous melanoma</h4>

1268<p id="_1090" tabindex="-1">

1269The Cancer Genome Atlas (TCGA) Network performed an integrative multiplatform characterization of 333 cutaneous melanomas from 331 patients.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

12701</a>

1271] Using six types of molecular analysis at the DNA, RNA, and protein levels, the researchers identified four major genomic subtypes:</p>

1272<div class="pdq-content-list">

1273<ul id="_1091">

1274<li>

1275<em class="gene-name">

1276BRAF</em>

1277 mutant.</li>

1278<li>

1279<em class="gene-name">

1280RAS</em>

1281 mutant.</li>

1282<li>

1283<em class="gene-name">

1284NF1</em>

1285 mutant.</li>

1286<li>

1287Triple wild-type.</li>

1288</ul>

1289</div>

1290<p id="_1092" tabindex="-1">

1291 Genomic subtypes may suggest drug targets and clinical trial design, as well as guide clinical decision-making for targeted therapies. For more information, see <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1100">

1292Table 1</a>

1293.</p>

1294<p id="_1093" tabindex="-1">

1295To date, targeted therapies have demonstrated efficacy and received U.S. Food and Drug Administration approval only for the <em class="gene-name">

1296BRAF</em>

1297-mutant subtype of melanoma. Combination therapies with a BRAF plus a MEK inhibitor have shown improvement in outcomes over a single-agent inhibitor alone; yet, virtually all patients acquire resistance to therapy and relapse. Therefore, clinical trials remain an important option for patients with <em class="gene-name">

1298BRAF</em>

1299-mutant subtype, as well as other genomic subtypes of melanoma. See the individual <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_885">

1300treatment sections</a>

1301 for more information.</p>

1302<p id="_1094" tabindex="-1">

1303A variety of immunotherapies have been approved for the treatment of melanoma regardless of genetic subtype. The benefit of immunotherapy has not been associated with a specific mutation or molecular subtype. The TCGA analysis identified immune markers (in a subset within each molecular subtype) that were associated with improved survival and that may have implications for immunotherapy. Identification of predictive biomarkers remains an active area of research. See the individual <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_885">

1304treatment sections</a>

1305 for more information. </p>

1538<section id="_1096">

1539<h4 id="_1096_toc">

1540Uveal melanoma</h4>

1541<p id="_1097" tabindex="-1">

1542Uveal melanomas differ significantly from cutaneous melanomas. ln one series, 83% of 186 uveal melanomas were found to have a constitutively active somatic mutation in <em class="gene-name">

1543GNAQ</em>

1544 or <em class="gene-name">

1545GNA11</em>

1546.[<a href="#cit/section_2.2">

15472</a>

1548,<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

15493</a>

1550] For more information, see <a href="/types/eye/hp/intraocular-melanoma-treatment-pdq">

1551Intraocular (Uveal) Melanoma Treatment</a>

1552.</p>

1553</section>

N Engl J Med 363 (23): 2191-9, 2010.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=21083380&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=21083380&amp;dopt=Abstract">

1568[PUBMED Abstract]</a>

1569</li>

1570</ol>

1571</div>

1572

1573 </section>

1574

1575

1576

1577 <section id="_884">

1578

1579 <h2>

1580Stage Information for Melanoma</h2>

1581

1582 <div id="_section_884" class="pdq-sections">

1583<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

1584<h6>

1585In This Section</h6>

1586<ul>

1587<li>

1588<a href="#_39_toc">

1589Clark Classification (Level of Invasion)</a>

1590</li>

1591<li>

1592<a href="#_41_toc">

1593AJCC Stage Groupings and TNM Definitions</a>

1594</li>

1595</ul>

1596</nav>

1597<p id="_522" tabindex="-1">

1598Clinical staging is based on whether the tumor has spread to regional lymph nodes or distant sites. For melanoma that is clinically confined to the primary site, the chance of lymph node or systemic metastases increases as the thickness and depth of local invasion increases, which worsens the prognosis. Melanoma can spread by local extension (through lymphatics) and/or by hematogenous routes to distant sites. Any organ may be involved by metastases, but the lungs and liver are common sites.</p>

1599<p id="_322" tabindex="-1">

1600The microstage of malignant melanoma is determined on histological examination by the vertical thickness of the lesion in millimeters (Breslow classification) and/or the anatomical level of local invasion (Clark classification). The Breslow thickness is more reproducible and more accurately predicts subsequent behavior of malignant melanoma in lesions thicker than 1.5 mm and should always be reported.</p>

1601<p id="_560" tabindex="-1">

1602Accurate microstaging of the primary tumor requires careful histological evaluation of the entire specimen by an experienced pathologist.</p>

1603<section id="_39">

1604<h3 id="_39_toc">

1605Clark Classification (Level of Invasion)</h3>

1606<table id="_40" class="table-default expandable-container">

1607<caption>

1608Table 2. Clark Classification (Level of Invasion)</caption>

1609<colgroup>

1610<col width="50.00%">

1618Description</th>

1619</tr>

1620</THead>

1621<tbody>

1622<tr>

1623<td>

1624Level I</td>

1625<td>

1626Lesions involving only the epidermis (<em>

1627in situ</em>

1628 melanoma); not an invasive lesion.

1629</td>

1630</tr>

1631<tr>

1632<td>

1633Level II</td>

1634<td>

1635Invasion of the papillary dermis; does not reach the

1636papillary-reticular dermal interface.</td>

1637</tr>

1638<tr>

1639<td>

1640Level III</td>

1641<td>

1642Invasion fills and expands the papillary dermis but does not

1643penetrate the reticular dermis.</td>

1644</tr>

1645<tr>

1646<td>

1647Level IV</td>

1648<td>

1649Invasion into the reticular dermis but not into the subcutaneous

1650tissue.</td>

1651</tr>

1652<tr>

1653<td>

1654Level V</td>

1655<td>

1656Invasion through the reticular dermis into the subcutaneous tissue.

1657</td>

1658</tr>

1659</tbody>

1660</table>

1661</section>

1662<section id="_41">

1663<h3 id="_41_toc">

1664AJCC Stage Groupings and TNM Definitions</h3>

1665<p id="_42" tabindex="-1">

1666 The American Joint Committee on Cancer (AJCC) has designated staging by TNM (tumor, node, metastasis) classification to define melanoma.[<a href="#cit/section_3.1">

16671</a>

1668]</p>

1669<p id="_1215" tabindex="-1">

1670Cancers staged using this staging system include cutaneous melanoma. Cancers not staged using this system include melanoma of the conjunctiva; melanoma of the uvea; mucosal melanoma arising in the head and neck; mucosal melanoma of the urethra, vagina, rectum, and anus; Merkel cell carcinoma; and squamous cell carcinoma.[<a href="#cit/section_3.1">

16711</a>

1672]</p>

1673<p id="_1212" tabindex="-1">

2738N2c = One clinically occult or clinically detected node/in-transit, satellite, and/or microsatellite metastases present.</td>

2739</tr>

2740<tr>

2741<td rowspan="3">

2742IIID</td>

2743<td rowspan="3">

2744T4b, N3a/b/c, M0</td>

2745<td rowspan="3">

2746T4b = &gt;4.0 mm/with ulceration.</td>

2747<td>

2748N3a = Four or more clinically occult nodes<span class="sup">

2749b</span>

2750/in-transit, satellite, and/or microsatellite metastases not present.</td>

2751<td rowspan="3">

2752M0 = No evidence of distant metastasis.</td>

2753</tr>

2754<tr>

2755<td>

2756N3b = Four or more nodes, at least one of which was clinically detected, or presence of any number of matted nodes/in-transit, satellite, and/or microsatellite metastases not present.</td>

2757</tr>

2758<tr>

2759<td>

2760N3c = Two or more clinically occult or clinically detected nodes and/or presence of any number of matted nodes/in-transit, satellite, and/or microsatellite metastases present. </td>

2761</tr>

2762</tbody>

2763</table>

3044<section id="_368">

3045<h3 id="_368_toc">

3046Excision</h3>

3047<p id="_369" tabindex="-1">

3048Surgical excision remains the primary modality for treating melanoma. Cutaneous melanomas that have not spread beyond the initial site are highly curable. The treatment for localized melanoma is surgical excision with margins proportional to the microstage of the primary lesion.</p>

3049<section id="_753">

3050<h4 id="_753_toc">

3051Lymph node management</h4>

3052<section id="_905">

3053<h5 id="_905_toc">

3054Sentinel lymph node biopsy (SLNB)</h5>

3055<p id="_906" tabindex="-1">

3056Lymphatic mapping and SLNB can be considered to assess the presence of occult metastasis in the regional lymph nodes of patients with primary tumors larger than 1 to 4 mm, potentially identifying individuals who may be spared the morbidity of regional lymph node dissections and individuals who may benefit from adjuvant therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_4.1">

30571</a>

3058-<a href="#cit/section_4.6">

30596</a>

3060]</p>

3061<p id="_907" tabindex="-1">

3062To ensure accurate identification of the sentinel lymph node, lymphatic mapping and removal of the SLN should precede wide excision of the primary melanoma.</p>

3063<p id="_908" tabindex="-1">

3064Multiple studies have demonstrated the diagnostic accuracy of SLNB, with false-negative rates of 0% to 2%.[<a href="#cit/section_4.1">

30651</a>

3066,<a href="#cit/section_4.6">

30676</a>

3068-<a href="#cit/section_4.11">

306911</a>

3070] If metastatic melanoma is detected, a complete regional lymphadenectomy can be performed in a second procedure. </p>

3071</section>

3072<section id="_909">

3073<h5 id="_909_toc">

3074Complete lymph node dissection (CLND)</h5>

3075<p id="_910" tabindex="-1">

3076Patients can be considered for CLND if the sentinel node(s) is microscopically or macroscopically positive for regional control or considered for entry into the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00297895">

3077Multicenter Selective Lymphadenectomy Trial II</a>

3078 (NCT00297895) to determine whether CLND affects survival. SLNB should be performed before wide excision of the primary melanoma to ensure accurate lymphatic mapping.</p>

3079</section>

3080</section>

3081</section>

3082<section id="_900">

3083<h3 id="_900_toc">

3084Adjuvant Therapy</h3>

3085<p id="NCT00636168" tabindex="-1">

3086Adjuvant therapy options are expanding for patients at high risk of recurrence after complete resection and include checkpoint inhibitors and combination signal transduction inhibitor therapy. Ipilimumab was the first checkpoint inhibitor to be approved by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) as adjuvant therapy, and it has demonstrated improved overall survival (OS) at 10 mg/kg (ipi10) compared with placebo (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00636168">

3087EORTC 18071</a>

3088 [NCT00636168]).[<a href="#cit/section_4.12">

308912</a>

3090] However, ipi10 has significant toxicity at this dose. The North American Intergroup Trial <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01274338">

3091E1609</a>

3092 (NCT01274338), designed with three treatment groups, compared ipi10 with ipilimumab at a lower dose of 3 mg/kg (ipi3) (approved for metastatic melanoma) and with high-dose interferon (HDI). Ipi3 showed a significant improvement in OS whereas ipi10 did not.[<a href="#cit/section_4.13">

309313</a>

3094] These data remove support for HDI as adjuvant treatment of melanoma. As newer checkpoint inhibitors emerge, the role of ipi3 remains to be further defined.</p>

3095<p id="_1270" tabindex="-1">

3096Large randomized trials with the newer checkpoint inhibitors (nivolumab and pembrolizumab) and with combination signal transduction inhibitors (dabrafenib plus trametinib) showed a clinically significant impact on relapse-free survival (RFS). <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02388906">

3097CheckMate 238</a>

3098 (NCT02388906) compared nivolumab with ipi10 and found that nivolumab was superior in RFS and had a more tolerable safety profile.[<a href="#cit/section_4.14">

309914</a>

3100] Pembrolizumab was superior to placebo in RFS, with data on OS still maturing in the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02362594">

3101MK-3475-054/KEYNOTE-054</a>

3102 trial (NCT02362594).[<a href="#cit/section_4.15">

310315</a>

3104] Dabrafenib plus trametinib was superior to placebo in RFS, with data on OS still maturing in the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01682083">

3105COMBI-AD</a>

3106 trial (NCT01682083).[<a href="#cit/section_4.16">

310716</a>

3108] Single-agent BRAF-inhibitor therapy with vemurafenib did not show improved RFS compared with placebo in the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01667419">

3109BRIM8</a>

3110 trial (NCT01667419).[<a href="#cit/section_4.17">

311117</a>

3112]</p>

3113<p id="_1271" tabindex="-1">

3114The benefit of immunotherapy with ipilimumab, nivolumab, and pembrolizumab has been seen regardless of programmed death-ligand 1 (PD-L1) expression or <em class="gene-name">

3115BRAF</em>

3116 mutations. Combination signal transduction inhibitor therapy is an additional option for patients with <em class="gene-name">

3117BRAF</em>

3118 mutations.</p>

3119<p id="_1272" tabindex="-1">

3120Participation in clinical trials designed to identify treatments that will further extend RFS and OS with less toxicity and shorter treatment schedules is an important option for all patients.</p>

3121</section>

3122<section id="_762">

3123<h3 id="_762_toc">

3124Limb Perfusion</h3>

3125<p id="_763" tabindex="-1">

3126 A completed, multicenter, phase III randomized trial (SWOG-8593) of patients with high-risk primary stage I limb melanoma did not show a disease-free survival or OS benefit from isolated limb perfusion with melphalan, when compared with surgery alone.[<a href="#cit/section_4.5">

31275</a>

3128]</p>

3129</section>

3130<section id="_857">

3131<h3 id="_857_toc">

3132Systematic Treatment for Unresectable Stage III, Stage IV, and Recurrent Disease</h3>

3133<p id="_858" tabindex="-1">

3134Although melanoma that has spread to distant sites is rarely curable, treatment options are rapidly expanding. Two approaches&#8212;checkpoint inhibition and targeting the mitogen-activated protein kinase pathway&#8212;have demonstrated improvement in OS in randomized trials. Given the rapid development of new agents and combinations, patients and their physicians are encouraged to consider treatment in a clinical trial for initial treatment and at the time of progression.</p>

3135<section id="_859">

3136<h4 id="_859_toc">

3137 Immunotherapy</h4>

3138<section id="_1049">

3139<h5 id="_1049_toc">

3140Checkpoint inhibitors</h5>

3141<p id="_1050" tabindex="-1">

3142The FDA has approved three checkpoint inhibitors: pembrolizumab, nivolumab, and ipilimumab. Each has demonstrated the ability to impact OS against different comparators in unresectable or advanced disease. For more information, see the sections on <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_935">

3143Pembrolizumab</a>

3144, <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_964">

3145Nivolumab</a>

3146, and <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1061">

3147Ipilimumab</a>

3148. Multiple phase III trials are in progress to determine optimal sequencing of immunotherapies, immunotherapy with targeted therapy, and whether combinations of immunotherapies or immunotherapy plus targeted therapy are superior for increasing OS.</p>

3149</section>

3150<section id="_1051">

3151<h5 id="_1051_toc">

3152Interleukin-2 (IL-2)</h5>

3153<p id="_1052" tabindex="-1">

3154The FDA approved IL-2 in 1998 because of durable complete response (CR) rates in a minority of patients (6%&#8211;7%) with previously treated metastatic melanoma in eight phase I and II studies. Phase III trials comparing high-dose IL-2 with other treatments and providing an assessment of relative impact on OS have not been conducted.</p>

3155</section>

3156<section id="_1293">

3157<h5 id="_1293_toc">

3158Dual checkpoint inhibition</h5>

3159<p id="_1294" tabindex="-1">

3160The combination of anti&#8211;programmed death-1 (PD-1) and anti&#8211;cytotoxic T-lymphocyte antigen-4 (CTLA-4) immunotherapies (nivolumab and ipilimumab) has demonstrated prolongation of progression-free survival (PFS) and OS compared with ipilimumab monotherapy, but the combination is associated with significant toxicity.</p>

3161</section>

3162</section>

3163<section id="_862">

3164<h4 id="_862_toc">

3165Signal transduction inhibitors</h4>

3166<p id="_863" tabindex="-1">

3167Studies to date indicate that both BRAF and MEK inhibitors can significantly impact the natural history of melanoma, although they do not appear to be curative as single agents. Two combination regimens of BRAF and MEK inhibitors have demonstrated improved PFS and OS compared with BRAF inhibitor monotherapy.</p>

3168<section id="_882">

3169<h5 id="_882_toc">

3170BRAF inhibitors</h5>

3171<section id="_865">

3172<h6 id="_865_toc">

3173Vemurafenib</h6>

3174<p id="_866" tabindex="-1">

3175Vemurafenib, approved by the FDA in 2011, has shown an improvement in PFS and OS in patients with unresectable or advanced disease. Vemurafenib is an orally available, small-molecule, selective BRAF V600E kinase inhibitor, and its indication is limited to patients with a demonstrated <em class="gene-name">

3176BRAF</em>

3177 V600E mutation by an FDA-approved test.[<a href="#cit/section_4.11">

317811</a>

3179]</p>

3180</section>

3181<section id="_867">

3182<h6 id="_867_toc">

3183Dabrafenib</h6>

3184<p id="_868" tabindex="-1">

3185Dabrafenib is an orally available, small-molecule, selective BRAF inhibitor that was approved by the FDA in 2013. It showed improvement in PFS when compared with dacarbazine in an international multicenter trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01227889">

3186BREAK-3</a>

3187 [NCT01227889]).</p>

3188</section>

3189</section>

3190<section id="_869">

3191<h5 id="_869_toc">

3192MEK inhibitors</h5>

3193<section id="_870">

3194<h6 id="_870_toc">

3195Trametinib</h6>

3196<p id="_871" tabindex="-1">

3197Trametinib is an orally available, small-molecule, selective inhibitor of MEK1 and MEK2. The FDA approved trametinib in 2013 for patients with unresectable or metastatic melanoma with <em class="gene-name">

3198BRAF</em>

3199 V600E or K mutations. Trametinib demonstrated improved PFS over dacarbazine.</p>

3200</section>

3201<section id="_960">

3202<h6 id="_960_toc">

3203Cobimetinib</h6>

3204<p id="_961" tabindex="-1">

3205Cobimetinib is an orally available, small-molecule, selective MEK inhibitor. The FDA approved cobimetinib in 2015 for use in combination with the BRAF inhibitor vemurafenib. For more information, see the <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_872">

3206Combination signal transduction inhibitor therapy</a>

3207 section. </p>

3208</section>

3209</section>

3210<section id="_962">

3211<h5 id="_962_toc">

3212c-KIT inhibitors</h5>

3213<p id="_963" tabindex="-1">

3214Early data suggest that mucosal or acral melanomas with activating mutations or amplifications in <em class="gene-name">

3215c-KIT</em>

3216 may be sensitive to a variety of c-KIT inhibitors.[<a href="#cit/section_4.18">

321718</a>

3218-<a href="#cit/section_4.20">

321920</a>

3220] Phase II and phase III trials are available for patients with unresectable stage III or stage IV melanoma harboring the <em class="gene-name">

3221c-KIT</em>

3222 mutation.</p>

3223</section>

3224<section id="_872">

3225<h5 id="_872_toc">

3226Combination signal transduction inhibitor therapy</h5>

3227<p id="_873" tabindex="-1">

3228The FDA approved two combination regimens, dabrafenib plus trametinib and vemurafenib plus cobimetinib, in patients with unresectable or metastatic melanomas that carry the <em class="gene-name">

3229BRAF</em>

3230 V600E or V600K mutation as confirmed by an FDA-approved test. The approvals were based on improved PFS and OS when compared with a single-agent BRAF inhibitor (either dabrafenib or vemurafenib). </p>

3231</section>

3232<section id="_1295">

3233<h5 id="_1295_toc">

3234Combination signal transduction inhibitor therapy plus anti-PD-L1 therapy</h5>

3235<p id="_1296" tabindex="-1">

3236The triplet regimen of cobimetinib (MEK inhibitor), vemurafenib (BRAF kinase inhibitor), and atezolizumab (PD-L1 inhibitor) showed improved PFS over the combination of cobimetinib and vemurafenib.[<a href="#cit/section_4.21">

323721</a>

3238]</p>

3239</section>

3240</section>

3241<section id="_876">

3242<h4 id="_876_toc">

3243Chemotherapy</h4>

3244<section id="_1054">

3245<h5 id="_1054_toc">

3246Dacarbazine</h5>

3247<p id="_1055" tabindex="-1">

3248Dacarbazine was approved in 1970 on the basis of overall response rates. Phase III trials indicated an overall response rate of 10% to 20%, with rare CRs observed. An impact on OS has not been demonstrated in randomized trials.[<a href="#cit/section_4.22">

324922</a>

3250-<a href="#cit/section_4.25">

325125</a>

3252] When used as a control arm for recent registration trials of ipilimumab and vemurafenib in previously untreated patients with metastatic melanoma, dacarbazine was shown to be inferior for OS.</p>

3253</section>

3254<section id="_1056">

3255<h5 id="_1056_toc">

3256Temozolomide</h5>

3257<p id="_1057" tabindex="-1">

3258Temozolomide, an oral alkylating agent, appeared to be similar to intravenous dacarbazine in a randomized phase III trial with a primary end point of OS. However, because the trial was designed to demonstrate the superiority of temozolomide, which was not achieved, the trial was left with a sample size that was inadequate to provide statistical proof of noninferiority.[<a href="#cit/section_4.23">

325923</a>

3260]</p>

3261</section>

3262</section>

3263<section id="_911">

3264<h4 id="_911_toc">

3265Palliative local therapy</h4>

3266<p id="_912" tabindex="-1">

3267Melanoma metastatic to distant, lymph node&#8211;bearing areas may be palliated by regional lymphadenectomy. Isolated metastases to the lung, gastrointestinal tract, bone, or sometimes the brain may be palliated by resection, with occasional long-term survival.[<a href="#cit/section_4.14">

326814</a>

3269,<a href="#cit/section_4.26">

327026</a>

3271,<a href="#cit/section_4.27">

327227</a>

3273]</p>

3274</section>

3275</section>

3420<section id="_60">

3421<h3 id="_60_toc">

3422Standard Treatment Options for Stage 0 Melanoma</h3>

3424Standard treatment options for stage 0 melanoma include the following:</p>

3425<div class="pdq-content-list">

3426<ol id="_62">

3433<section id="_596">

3434<h4 id="_596_toc">

3435Excision</h4>

3436<p id="_63" tabindex="-1">

3437Patients with stage 0 disease may be treated by excision with minimal, but

3438microscopically free, margins.</p>

3439</section>

3440</section>

3442<h3 id="_TrialSearch_886_sid_5_toc">

3445Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

3446advanced clinical trial search</a>

3447 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

3448General information</a>

3449 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

3487<section id="_597">

3488<h3 id="_597_toc">

3489Standard Treatment Options for Stage I Melanoma</h3>

3490<p id="_66" tabindex="-1">

3491Standard treatment options for stage I melanoma include the following:</p>

3492<div class="pdq-content-list">

3493<ol id="_311">

3494<li>

3495<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_65">

3496Excision</a>

3497 with or without <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_599">

3498lymph node management</a>

3499.</li>

3500</ol>

3501</div>

3502<section id="_65">

3503<h4 id="_65_toc">

3504Excision</h4>

3505<p id="_68" tabindex="-1">

3506Evidence suggests that lesions no thicker than 2 mm may be treated conservatively with radial excision margins of 1 cm. </p>

3507<p id="_527" tabindex="-1">

3508Depending on the location of the melanoma, most patients can now have the excision performed on an outpatient basis.</p>

3509<p id="_69" tabindex="-1">

3510Evidence (excision):</p>

3511<div class="pdq-content-list">

3512<ol id="_70">

3513<li>

3514A randomized trial compared narrow margins (1 cm) with wide margins (&#8805;3 cm) in patients with melanomas no thicker than 2 mm.[<a href="#cit/section_6.1">

35151</a>

3516,<a href="#cit/section_6.2">

35172</a>

3518][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3519Level of evidence A1</a>

3520]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3521<ul id="_490">

3522<li>

3523No difference was observed between the two groups in the development of metastatic disease, disease-free survival (DFS), or overall survival (OS).</li>

3524</ul>

3525</div>

3526</li>

3527<li>

3528Two other randomized trials compared 2-cm margins with wider margins (4 cm or 5 cm).[<a href="#cit/section_6.3">

35293</a>

3530,<a href="#cit/section_6.4">

35314</a>

3532][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3533Level of evidence A1</a>

3534] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3535<ul id="_478">

3536<li>

3537No statistically significant difference in local recurrence, distant

3538metastasis, or OS was found; the median follow-up was at least 10 years for both trials.</li>

3539</ul>

3540</div>

3541</li>

3542<li>

3543In the Intergroup Melanoma Surgical Trial, the reduction in margins from 4 cm to 2 cm

3544was associated with both of the following:[<a href="#cit/section_6.5">

35455</a>

3546][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3547Level of evidence A1</a>

3548]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3549<ul id="_479">

3550<li>

3551A statistically significant reduction in the need for skin

3552grafting (from 46% to 11%; <em>

3553P</em>

3554 &lt; .001).</li>

3555<li>

3556A reduction in the length of hospital stay.</li>

3557</ul>

3558</div>

3559</li>

3560<li>

3561A multicenter, phase III randomized trial (SWOG-8593) of patients with high-risk stage I primary limb melanoma did not show a DFS or OS benefit from isolated limb perfusion with melphalan, when compared with surgery alone.[<a href="#cit/section_6.6">

35626</a>

3563,<a href="#cit/section_6.7">

35647</a>

3565] </li>

3566</ol>

3567</div>

3568<section id="_599">

3569<h5 id="_599_toc">

3570Lymph node management</h5>

3571<p id="_529" tabindex="-1">

3572Elective regional lymph node dissection is of no proven benefit for patients with stage I melanoma.[<a href="#cit/section_6.8">

35738</a>

3574]</p>

3575<p id="_530" tabindex="-1">

3576Lymphatic mapping and sentinel lymph node

3577biopsy (SLNB) for patients who have tumors of intermediate thickness and/or ulcerated tumors may identify individuals with occult nodal disease. These patients may benefit from regional lymphadenectomy and adjuvant therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.6">

35786</a>

3579,<a href="#cit/section_6.9">

35809</a>

3581-<a href="#cit/section_6.11">

358211</a>

3583]</p>

3584<p id="_76" tabindex="-1">

3585Evidence (immediate lymphadenectomy vs. observation with delayed lymphadenectomy):</p>

3586<div class="pdq-content-list">

3587<ol id="_77">

3588<li>

3589The International Multicenter Selective Lymphadenectomy Trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00275496">

3590MSLT-1</a>

3591 [JWCI-MORD-MSLT-1193]) included 1,269 patients with intermediate-thickness (defined as 1.2 mm&#8211;3.5 mm in this study) primary melanomas.[<a href="#cit/section_6.12">

359212</a>

3593][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3594Level of evidence A1</a>

3595]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3596<ul id="_480">

3597<li>

3598There was no melanoma-specific survival advantage (primary end point) for patients randomly assigned to undergo wide excision plus SLNB, followed by immediate complete lymphadenectomy for node positivity versus nodal observation and delayed lymphadenectomy for subsequent nodal recurrence at a median of 59.8 months.</li>

3599<li>

3600This trial was not designed to detect a difference in the impact of lymphadenectomy in patients with microscopic lymph node involvement.</li>

3601</ul>

3602</div>

3603</li>

3604<li>

3605The Sunbelt Melanoma Trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00004196">

3606UAB-9735</a>

3607 [NCT00004196]) was a phase III trial to determine the effects of lymphadenectomy with or without adjuvant high-dose interferon alpha-2b versus observation on DFS and OS in patients with submicroscopic sentinel lymph node (SLN) metastasis detected only by the polymerase chain reaction assay (i.e., SLN negative by histology and immunohistochemistry).<div class="pdq-content-list">

3608<ul id="_563">

3609<li>

3610No survival data have been reported from this study.</li>

3611</ul>

3612</div>

3613</li>

3614</ol>

3615</div>

3616</section>

3617</section>

3618</section>

3619<section id="_601">

3620<h3 id="_601_toc">

3621Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation for Stage I Melanoma</h3>

3622<p id="_80" tabindex="-1">

3623Treatment options under clinical evaluation for patients with stage I melanoma include the following:</p>

3624<div class="pdq-content-list">

3625<ol id="_81">

3626<li>

3627Clinical trials evaluating new techniques to detect submicroscopic SLN metastasis. Because of the higher rate of treatment failure in the subset of clinical stage I patients with occult nodal disease, clinical trials have evaluated new techniques to detect submicroscopic SLN metastasis to identify patients who may benefit from regional lymphadenectomy with or without adjuvant therapy.</li>

3628</ol>

3629</div>

3630</section>

3636advanced clinical trial search</a>

3637 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

3638General information</a>

3639 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

3704 <div id="_section_888" class="pdq-sections">

3706<h6>

3707In This Section</h6>

3708<ul>

3709<li>

3710<a href="#_598_toc">

3711Standard Treatment Options for Stage II Melanoma<ul>

3712<li>

3713<a href="#_87_toc">

3714Excision</a>

3715</li>

3716</ul>

3717</a>

3718</li>

3719<li>

3720<a href="#_117_toc">

3721Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation for Stage II Melanoma</a>

3729<section id="_598">

3730<h3 id="_598_toc">

3731Standard Treatment Options for Stage II Melanoma</h3>

3732<p id="_88" tabindex="-1">

3733Standard treatment options for stage II melanoma include the following:</p>

3734<div class="pdq-content-list">

3735<ol id="_89">

3736<li>

3737<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_87">

3738Excision</a>

3739 with or without <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_603">

3740lymph node management</a>

3741.</li>

3742</ol>

3743</div>

3744<section id="_87">

3745<h4 id="_87_toc">

3746Excision</h4>

3747<p id="_353" tabindex="-1">

3748For melanomas with a thickness between 2 and 4 mm, surgical margins need to be 2 to 3 cm or smaller.</p>

3749<p id="_531" tabindex="-1">

3750Few data are available to guide treatment in patients with melanomas thicker than 4 mm; however, most guidelines recommend margins of 3 cm whenever anatomically possible. </p>

3751<p id="_670" tabindex="-1">

3752Depending on the location of the melanoma, most patients can have the excision performed on an outpatient basis.</p>

3753<p id="_354" tabindex="-1">

3754Evidence (excision):</p>

3755<div class="pdq-content-list">

3756<ol id="_92">

3757<li>

3758The Intergroup Melanoma Surgical Trial Task 2b compared 2-cm versus 4-cm margins for patients with melanomas that were 1 mm to 4 mm thick.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

37591</a>

3760]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3761<ul id="_482">

3762<li>

3763With a median follow-up of more than 10 years, no significant difference in local recurrence or survival was observed between the two groups.</li>

3764<li>

3765The

3766reduction in margins from 4 cm to 2 cm was associated with the following:<div class="pdq-content-list">

3767<ul id="_483" class="list-dash">

3768<li>

3769A

3770statistically significant reduction in the need for skin grafting (from 46% to 11%; <em>

3771P</em>

3772 &lt; .001).</li>

3773<li>

3774A reduction in the length of the hospital stay.</li>

3775</ul>

3776</div>

3777</li>

3778</ul>

3779</div>

3780</li>

3781<li>

3782A study conducted in the United Kingdom randomly assigned patients with melanomas thicker than 2 mm to undergo excision with either 1-cm or 3-cm margins.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

37832</a>

3784]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3785<ul id="_484">

3786<li>

3787Patients treated with excision with 1-cm margins had higher rates of local regional recurrence (hazard ratio [HR], 1.26; 95% confidence interval [CI], 1.00&#8211;1.59; <em>

3788P</em>

3789 = .05).</li>

3790<li>

3791No difference in survival was seen (HR, 1.24; 95% CI, 0.96&#8211;1.61; <em>

3792P</em>

3793 = .1).</li>

3794<li>

3795This study suggests that 1-cm margins may not be adequate for patients with melanomas thicker than 2 mm.</li>

3796</ul>

3797</div>

3798</li>

3799</ol>

3800</div>

3801<section id="_603">

3802<h5 id="_603_toc">

3803Lymph node management</h5>

3804<section id="_604">

3805<h6 id="_604_toc">

3806Lymphatic mapping and sentinel lymph node biopsy (SLNB)</h6>

3807<p id="_99" tabindex="-1">

3808Lymphatic mapping and SLNB have been used to assess the

3809presence of occult metastasis in the regional lymph nodes of patients with

3810stage II disease, potentially identifying individuals who may be spared the

3811morbidity of regional lymph node dissections (LNDs) and individuals who may benefit

3812from adjuvant therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

38133</a>

3814-<a href="#cit/section_7.7">

38157</a>

3816]</p>

3817<p id="_572" tabindex="-1">

3818To ensure accurate identification of the sentinel lymph node, lymphatic mapping and removal of the SLN should precede wide excision of the primary melanoma.</p>

3819<p id="_555" tabindex="-1">

3820With the use of a vital blue dye and a radiopharmaceutical agent injected at the site of the primary tumor, the first lymph node in the lymphatic basin that drains the lesion can be identified, removed, and examined microscopically. Multiple studies have demonstrated the diagnostic accuracy of SLNB, with false-negative rates of 0% to 2%.[<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

38213</a>

3822,<a href="#cit/section_7.8">

38238</a>

3824-<a href="#cit/section_7.12">

382512</a>

3826] If metastatic melanoma is detected, a complete regional lymphadenectomy can be performed in a second procedure.</p>

3827</section>

3828<section id="_605">

3829<h6 id="_605_toc">

3830Regional lymphadenectomy</h6>

3831<p id="_102" tabindex="-1">

3832No published data on the clinical

3833significance of micrometastatic melanoma in regional lymph nodes are available from prospective trials. Some evidence suggests that for patients with tumors of intermediate thickness and

3834occult metastasis, survival is better among patients who undergo

3835immediate regional lymphadenectomy than it is among those who delay lymphadenectomy

3836until the clinical appearance of nodal metastasis.[<a href="#cit/section_7.13">

383713</a>

3838] This finding should be viewed with caution because it

3839arose from a post hoc subset analysis of data from a randomized trial.</p>

3840<p id="_104" tabindex="-1">

3841Evidence (regional lymphadenectomy):</p>

3842<div class="pdq-content-list">

3843<ol id="_105">

3844<li>

3845The International Multicenter Selective Lymphadenectomy Trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00275496">

3846MSLT-1</a>

3847 [JWCI-MORD-MSLT-1193]) included 1,269 patients with intermediate-thickness (defined as 1.2 mm&#8211;3.5 mm in this study) primary melanomas.[<a href="#cit/section_7.14">

384814</a>

3849][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3850Level of evidence A1</a>

3851]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3852<ul id="_485">

3853<li>

3854There was no melanoma-specific survival advantage (primary end point) for patients randomly assigned to undergo wide excision plus SLNB, followed by immediate complete lymphadenectomy for node positivity versus nodal observation and delayed lymphadenectomy for subsequent nodal recurrence at a median of 59.8 months.</li>

3855<li>

3856This trial was not designed to detect a difference in the impact of lymphadenectomy in patients with microscopic lymph node involvement.</li>

3857</ul>

3858</div>

3859</li>

3860<li>

3861Three other prospective randomized trials have failed to show a survival benefit for prophylactic regional LNDs.[<a href="#cit/section_7.15">

386215</a>

3863-<a href="#cit/section_7.17">

386417</a>

3865]</li>

3866</ol>

3867</div>

3868</section>

3869</section>

3870</section>

3871</section>

3872<section id="_117">

3873<h3 id="_117_toc">

3874Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation for Stage II Melanoma</h3>

3875<p id="_536" tabindex="-1">

3876Postsurgical systemic adjuvant treatment has not been adequately studied in patients with stage II disease; therefore, clinical trials are an important therapeutic option for patients at high risk of relapse.</p>

3877</section>

3883advanced clinical trial search</a>

3884 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

3885General information</a>

3886 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

J Am Acad Dermatol 44 (5): 762-6, 2001.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=11312421&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=11312421&amp;dopt=Abstract">

4000<section id="_403">

4001<h3 id="_403_toc">

4002Standard Treatment Options for Resectable Stage III Melanoma</h3>

4003<p id="_127" tabindex="-1">

4004Standard treatment options for <strong>

4005resectable</strong>

4006 stage III melanoma include the following:</p>

4007<div class="pdq-content-list">

4008<ol id="_607">

4009<li>

4010 <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_626">

4011Excision</a>

4012 with or without <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_913">

4013lymph node management</a>

4014.</li>

4015<li>

4016<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_775">

4017Adjuvant therapy</a>

4018.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4019<ol id="_1107" class="lower-alpha">

4020<li>

4021 <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1020">

4022 Immunotherapy</a>

4023.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4024<ul id="_1108">

4025<li>

4026<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1102">

4027Checkpoint inhibitors</a>

4028.</li>

4029</ul>

4030</div>

4031</li>

4032<li>

4033<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1112">

4034Combination signal transduction inhibitors</a>

4035. <div class="pdq-content-list">

4036<ul id="_1111">

4037<li>

4038<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1113">

4039Dabrafenib plus trametinib</a>

4040.</li>

4041</ul>

4042</div>

4043</li>

4044</ol>

4045</div>

4046</li>

4047</ol>

4048</div>

4049<section id="_626">

4050<h4 id="_626_toc">

4051Excision</h4>

4052<p id="_540" tabindex="-1">

4053The primary tumor may be treated with wide local excision with 1 to 3-cm margins, depending on tumor thickness and location.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

40541</a>

4055-<a href="#cit/section_8.7">

40567</a>

4057] Skin grafting may be necessary to close the resulting defect. </p>

4058<section id="_913">

4059<h5 id="_913_toc">

4060Lymph node management</h5>

4061<section id="_918">

4062<h6 id="_918_toc">

4063Sentinel lymph node biopsy (SLNB)</h6>

4064<p id="_919" tabindex="-1">

4065Lymphatic mapping and SLNB can be considered to assess the presence of occult metastases in the regional lymph nodes of patients with primary tumors larger than 1 to 4 mm, potentially identifying individuals who may be spared the morbidity of regional lymph node dissections and individuals who may benefit from adjuvant therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_8.3">

40663</a>

4067,<a href="#cit/section_8.8">

40688</a>

4069-<a href="#cit/section_8.12">

407012</a>

4071]</p>

4072<p id="_920" tabindex="-1">

4073To ensure accurate identification of the sentinel lymph node (SLN), lymphatic mapping and removal of the SLN should precede wide excision of the primary melanoma.</p>

4074<p id="_921" tabindex="-1">

4075Multiple studies have demonstrated the diagnostic accuracy of SLNB, with false-negative rates of 0% to 2%.[<a href="#cit/section_8.8">

40768</a>

4077,<a href="#cit/section_8.12">

407812</a>

4079-<a href="#cit/section_8.17">

408017</a>

4081] If metastatic melanoma is detected, a complete regional lymphadenectomy can be performed in a second procedure. </p>

4082</section>

4083<section id="_922">

4084<h6 id="_922_toc">

4085Complete lymph node dissection (CLND) </h6>

4086<p id="_923" tabindex="-1">

4087Patients can be considered for CLND if the sentinel node(s) is microscopically or macroscopically positive for regional control or considered for entry into the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00297895">

4088Multicenter Selective Lymphadenectomy Trial II</a>

4089 (NCT00297895) to determine whether CLND affects survival. SLNB should be performed prior to wide excision of the primary melanoma to ensure accurate lymphatic mapping.</p>

4090</section>

4091</section>

4092</section>

4093<section id="_775">

4094<h4 id="_775_toc">

4095Adjuvant Therapy</h4>

4096<p id="_1019" tabindex="-1">

4097Adjuvant therapeutic options are expanding for patients at high risk of recurrence after complete resection and include checkpoint inhibitors and combination signal transduction inhibitor therapy. Ipilimumab was the first checkpoint inhibitor to be approved by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) as adjuvant therapy, and it has demonstrated improved overall survival (OS) at 10 mg/kg (ipi10) compared with placebo (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00636168">

4098EORTC 18071</a>

4099 [NCT00636168]).[<a href="#cit/section_8.18">

410018</a>

4101] However, ipi10 has significant toxicity at this dose. The North American Intergroup Trial <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01274338">

4102E1609</a>

4103 (NCT01274338), designed with three treatment groups, compared ipi10 with ipilimumab at a lower dose of 3 mg/kg (ipi3) (approved for metastatic disease) and with high-dose interferon (HDI). Ipi3 showed a significant improvement in OS whereas ipi10 did not.[<a href="#cit/section_8.19">

410419</a>

4105] These data remove support for HDI as adjuvant treatment for melanoma. As newer checkpoint inhibitors emerge, the role of ipi3 remains to be further defined.</p>

4106<p id="_1273" tabindex="-1">

4107Large randomized trials with the newer checkpoint inhibitors (nivolumab and pembrolizumab) and with combination signal transduction inhibitors (dabrafenib plus trametinib) showed a clinically significant impact on relapse-free survival (RFS). <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02388906">

4108CheckMate 238</a>

4109 (NCT02388906) compared nivolumab with ipi10 and found that nivolumab was superior in RFS and had a more tolerable safety profile.[<a href="#cit/section_8.20">

411020</a>

4111] Pembrolizumab was superior to placebo in RFS, with data on OS still maturing in the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02362594">

4112MK-3475-054/KEYNOTE-054</a>

4113 trial (NCT02362594).[<a href="#cit/section_8.21">

411421</a>

4115] Dabrafenib plus trametinib was superior to placebo in RFS, with data on OS still maturing in the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01682083">

4116COMBI-AD</a>

4117 trial (NCT01682083).[<a href="#cit/section_8.22">

411822</a>

4119] Single-agent BRAF-inhibitor therapy with vemurafenib did not show improved RFS compared with placebo in the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01667419">

4120BRIM8</a>

4121 trial (NCT01667419).[<a href="#cit/section_8.23">

412223</a>

4123]</p>

4124<p id="_1167" tabindex="-1">

4125The benefit of immunotherapy with ipilimumab, nivolumab, and pembrolizumab has been seen regardless of programmed death-ligand 1 (PD-L1) expression or <em class="gene-name">

4126BRAF</em>

4127 mutations. Combination signal transduction inhibitor therapy with dabrafenib plus trametinib is an additional option for patients with <em class="gene-name">

4128BRAF</em>

4129 mutations.</p>

4130<p id="_1169" tabindex="-1">

4131Participation in clinical trials to identify treatments that will further extend RFS and OS with less toxicity and shorter treatment schedules is an important option for all patients.</p>

4132<section id="_1020">

4133<h5 id="_1020_toc">

4134Immunotherapy</h5>

4135<section id="_1102">

4136<h6 id="_1102_toc">

4137Checkpoint inhibitors</h6>

4138<section id="_1103">

4139<h6 id="_1103_toc">

4140Nivolumab</h6>

4141<p id="_1104" tabindex="-1">

4142Evidence (nivolumab):</p>

4143<div class="pdq-content-list">

4144<ol id="_1105">

4145<li>

4146 In a multinational, randomized, double-blind trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02388906">

4147CheckMate 238</a>

4148 [NCT02388906]), patients with stage IIIB, IIIC, or IV melanoma who underwent complete resection were randomly assigned (1:1) to receive either nivolumab or ipilimumab.[<a href="#cit/section_8.20">

414920</a>

4150][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4151Level of evidence B1</a>

4152] The primary end point was RFS and was defined as time from randomization until the date of the first recurrence, new primary melanoma, or death from any cause. Patients who were excluded included those with resection occurring more than 12 weeks before randomization, autoimmune disease, use of systemic glucocorticoids, previous systemic therapy for melanoma, and an Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group (ECOG) Performance Status (PS) score higher than 1. Nivolumab was administered at the dose of 3 mg/kg intravenously (IV) every 2 weeks and ipilimumab was administered at the dose of 10 mg/kg every 3 weeks for four doses, then every 3 months for up to 1 year or

4153until disease recurrence, along with corresponding placebo. <p id="_1174" tabindex="-1">

4154A total of 906 patients were randomly assigned: 453 patients to nivolumab and 453 patients to ipilimumab. Baseline characteristics were balanced. Approximately 81% of patients had stage III disease, 32% had ulcerated primary melanoma, 48% had macroscopic lymph node involvement, 62% had less than a 5% PD-L1 expression, and 42% harbored <em class="gene-name">

4155BRAF</em>

4156 mutations.</p>

4157<div class="pdq-content-list">

4158<ul id="_1106">

4159<li>

4160The European Organisation for Research and Treatment of Cancer (EORTC) Independent Data Monitoring Committee stopped the study at the protocol-specified interim analysis, when all patients had a minimum follow-up of 18 months, at which time there were 360 events of RFS. The median RFS has not been reached in either treatment group. At 12 months, the rate of RFS for patients treated with nivolumab was 70.5% (95% confidence interval [CI], 66.1%&#8211;74.0%) versus 60.8% (95% CI, 56.0%&#8211;65.2%) in patients treated with ipilimumab. Recurrence or death occurred in 34% (154 of 453) of patients treated with nivolumab versus 45.5% (206 of 453) of patients treated with ipilimumab (hazard ratio [HR] <sub>

4161recurrence or death</sub>

4162, 0.65; 97.56% CI, 0.51&#8211;0.83; <em>

4163P</em>

4164 &lt; .001). Subgroup analyses of RFS favored nivolumab regardless of PD-L1 expression or <em class="gene-name">

4165BRAF</em>

4166 V600 mutation.</li>

4167<li>

4168Patients treated with nivolumab had fewer adverse events (AEs), including grade 3 to 4 serious AEs and death. Nivolumab was discontinued in 9.7% of patients, and ipilimumab was discontinued in 42.6% of patients because of AEs. Two treatment-related deaths occurred among patients treated with ipilimumab (e.g., marrow aplasia and colitis) and none occurred among the patients treated with nivolumab. The AE profile was like the type of checkpoint inhibitor toxicities seen in the metastatic setting, with immune-related events most commonly seen in the gastrointestinal system, hepatic system, and skin. Grade 3 or 4 AEs occurred in 14% of patients treated with nivolumab and in 46% of patients treated with ipilimumab.</li>

4169<li>

4170An updated analysis, after a minimum of 4 years of follow-up, showed an RFS of 51.7% (95% CI, 46.8%&#8211;56.3%) for patients who received nivolumab versus 41.2% (95% CI, 36.4%&#8211;45.9%) for patients who received ipilimumab (HR <sub>

4171relapse or death</sub>

4172, 0.71; 95% CI, 0.60&#8211;0.86; <em>

4173P</em>

4174 = .0003). Median OS has not been reached in either group.[<a href="#cit/section_8.24">

417524</a>

4176]

4177</li>

4178</ul>

4179</div>

4180</li>

4181</ol>

4182</div>

4183</section>

4184<section id="_1170">

4185<h6 id="_1170_toc">

4186Pembrolizumab</h6>

4187<p id="_1171" tabindex="-1">

4188Evidence (pembrolizumab):</p>

4189<div class="pdq-content-list">

4190<p class="pdq-list-title">

4191</p>

4192<ol id="_1172">

4193<li>

4194 In a multinational, randomized, double-blind trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02362594">

4195MK-3475-054/KEYNOTE-054</a>

4196 [NCT02362594]), patients with completely resected stage IIIA, IIIB, or IIIC melanoma were randomly assigned (1:1) to receive pembrolizumab or placebo.[<a href="#cit/section_8.21">

419721</a>

4198][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4199Level of evidence B1</a>

4200] The primary end point was RFS, defined as time from randomization until the date of first recurrence or death from any cause. If recurrence was documented, patients could cross over or repeat treatment with pembrolizumab. Pembrolizumab was given as an IV infusion of 200 mg every 3 weeks, for a total of 18 doses (approximately 1 year).<p id="_1175" tabindex="-1">

4201 A total of 1,019 patients were randomly assigned: 514 to pembrolizumab and 505 to placebo. Baseline characteristics were balanced. Approximately 40% had ulcerated primary melanoma, 66% had macroscopic lymph node involvement, 84% had positive PD-L1 expression (melanoma score &gt;2 by 22C3 antibody assay), and 44% harbored <em class="gene-name">

4202BRAF</em>

4203 mutations.</p>

4204<div class="pdq-content-list">

4205<ul id="_1173">

4206<li>

4207 The EORTC Independent Data Monitoring Committee reviewed the unblinded results at an amended interim analysis when 351 events (recurrences or deaths) had occurred. The results were positive, and the interim analysis of RFS became the final analysis. </li>

4208<li>

4209 At the amended interim analysis with a median follow-up of 15 months, the 12-month rate of RFS was 75.4% (95% CI, 71.3%&#8211;78.9%) in the pembrolizumab group versus 61.0% (95% CI, 56.5%&#8211;65.1%) in the placebo group. </li>

4210<li>

4211An update of the primary end point of RFS with a median follow-up 3.5 years showed 59.8% (95% CI, 55.3%&#8211;64.1%) RFS in the pembrolizumab group versus 41.4% (95% CI, 39.2%&#8211;48.8%) in the placebo group (HR, 0.59; 95% CI, 0.49&#8211;0.73).[<a href="#cit/section_8.25">

421225</a>

4213]</li>

4214<li>

4215Pembrolizumab maintained its effect regardless of PD-L1 positive or negative expression or <em class="gene-name">

4216BRAF</em>

4217 mutation status.</li>

4218<li>

4219 Approximately 14% of patients discontinued pembrolizumab due to an AE. Grade 3, 4, or 5 AEs considered to be related to pembrolizumab occurred in 15% of patients. There was one death due to treatment (myositis).</li>

4220</ul>

4221</div>

4222</li>

4223</ol>

4224</div>

4225</section>

4226<section id="_1132">

4227<h6 id="_1132_toc">

4228Ipilimumab</h6>

4229<p id="_1133" tabindex="-1">

4230Evidence (ipilimumab):</p>

4231<div class="pdq-content-list">

4232<ol id="_1134">

4233<li>

4234The open-label, three-arm, North American Intergroup trial <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01274338">

4235E1609</a>

4236 (NCT01274338) compared two doses of ipilimumab with HDI as adjuvant therapy in high-risk patients with melanoma.[<a href="#cit/section_8.19">

423719</a>

4238] A total of 1,670 patients with resected disease (defined by the American Joint Committee on Cancer, 7th edition, as stage IIIB, IIIC, M1a, or M1b) were randomly assigned (1:1:1) to ipilimumab 3 mg/kg (ipi3) or ipilimumab 10 mg/kg (ipi10) every 3 weeks for four doses (induction), followed by the same dose every 12 weeks for four doses (maintenance), or HDI 20 million units/m<span class="sup">

42392</span>

4240 per day, 5 days per week for 4 weeks (induction), followed by 10 million units/m<span class="sup">

42412</span>

4242 daily subcutaneously every other day, 3 days per week for 48 weeks (maintenance).[<a href="#cit/section_8.19">

424319</a>

4244][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4245Level of evidence A1</a>

4246] <p id="_1274" tabindex="-1">

4247 The trial was designed with two coprimary end points, RFS and OS, with a hierarchic analysis to evaluate ipi3 versus HDI followed by ipi10 versus HDI. The time to event was longer than anticipated and the design was amended for a final analysis at a data cutoff date giving a median follow-up time of 57.4 months (range, 0.03 months&#8722;86.6 months). </p>

4248<div class="pdq-content-list">

4249<ul id="_1275">

4250<li>

4251 Ipi3 significantly improved OS compared with HDI (HR, 0.78; 95% repeated CI, 0.61&#8722;0.99; <em>

4252P</em>

4253 = .044), but not RFS (HR, 0.85; 95% CI, 0.66&#8722;1.09; <em>

4254P</em>

4255 = .065). </li>

4256<li>

4257 Ipi10 did not significantly improve OS or RFS compared with HDI (HR, 0.88; 95.6% CI, 0.69&#8722;1.12 and exploratory HR, 0.84; 99.4% CI, 0.65&#8722;1.09, respectively).</li>

4258<li>

4259 Salvage treatments were used in 69.7% of patients after ipi3, 51.6% of patients after ipi10, and 86.2% of patients after HDI.</li>

4260</ul>

4261</div>

4262<p id="_1276" tabindex="-1">

4263Toxicity with ipi3 was lower than with ipi10; however, both had treatment-related discontinuations and death.</p>

4264<div class="pdq-content-list">

4265<ul id="_1277">

4266<li>

4267 Treatment-related discontinuations were 34.9% in the ipi3 group and 54.1% in the ipi10 group.</li>

4268<li>

4269 There were three possibly treatment-related deaths in the ipi3 group, five in the ipi10 group, and two in the HDI group.</li>

4270</ul>

4271</div>

4272<p id="_1278" tabindex="-1">

4273 The study concluded that evidence no longer supports a role for HDI as adjuvant therapy for patients with high-risk melanoma. Further, ipi3 provides OS data superior to ipi10 compared with HDI. The role of ipilimumab as adjuvant monotherapy is unclear because CheckMate 238 demonstrated that nivolumab was superior to ipi10 in improving RFS, with OS data still maturing.</p>

4274</li>

4275<li>

4276In a multinational, randomized, double-blind trial (EORTC 18071 [NCT00636168]), patients with stage III melanoma, who had complete resection, were randomly assigned (1:1) to receive ipilimumab or placebo.[<a href="#cit/section_8.26">

427726</a>

4278][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4279Level of evidence B1</a>

4280] Patients with lymph node metastasis larger than 1 mm, in-transit metastasis, resection occurring more than 12 weeks before randomization, autoimmune disease, previous or concurrent immunosuppressive therapy, previous systemic therapy for melanoma, and an ECOG PS score of greater than 1 were excluded. The ipilimumab dose was 10 mg/kg every 3 weeks for four doses, then every 3 months for up to 3 years. The primary end point was RFS, defined as recurrence or death (regardless of cause), whichever came first, as assessed by an independent review committee.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4281<ul id="_1135">

4282<li>

4283A total of 951 patients were enrolled (475 patients to the ipilimumab arm and 476 patients to the placebo arm). The median age was 51 years, and 94% of the patients had a PS of 0. </li>

4284<li>

4285At a median follow-up of 2.7 years, there were 528 RFS events: 234 in the ipilimumab group (49%; 220 recurrences, 14 deaths) and 294 in the placebo group (62%; 289 recurrences, 5 deaths). Median RFS was 26 months for the ipilimumab group (95% CI, 19&#8211;39) versus 17 months for the placebo group (95% CI, 13&#8211;22). The HR was 0.75 (95% CI, 0.64&#8211;0.90; <em>

4286P</em>

4287 &lt; .002). The effect of ipilimumab was consistent across subgroups. </li>

4288<li>

4289Ipilimumab was discontinued for AEs in 52% of the patients. Patients received ipilimumab for a median of four doses; 36% of patients in the ipilimumab group stayed on treatment for more than 6 months, and 26% stayed on treatment for more than 1 year. Five patients died from drug-related events: three secondary to colitis, one with myocarditis, and one of multiorgan failure with Guillain-Barr&#233; syndrome. The most common AEs were gastrointestinal, hepatic, and endocrine in nature and included rash, fatigue, and headache.</li>

4290</ul>

4291</div>

4292<p id="_1279" tabindex="-1">

4293An updated analysis was performed at a median follow-up of 5.3 years.[<a href="#cit/section_8.18">

429418</a>

4295]</p>

4296<div class="pdq-content-list">

4297<ul id="_1280">

4298<li>

4299 The 5-year rate of RFS was 40.8% in patients treated with ipilimumab and 30.3% in patients who received the placebo (HR <sub>

4300recurrence or death</sub>

4301, 0.76; 95% CI, 0.64&#8211;0.89; <em>

4302P</em>

4303 &lt; .001) and the median RFS was 27.6% in patients treated with ipilimumab and 17.1% in patients who received the placebo.</li>

4304<li>

4305 The rate of OS, a secondary end point, at 5 years was 65.4% in patients treated with ipilimumab versus 54.4% in patients who received the placebo (HR<sub>

4306death</sub>

4307, 0.72; 95.1% CI, 0.58&#8211;0.88; <em>

4308P</em>

4309 = .001).</li>

4310</ul>

4311</div>

4312</li>

4313</ol>

4314</div>

4315<p id="_1281" tabindex="-1">

4316Data from this trial (EORTC 18071), which tested high-dose ipilimumab at 10 mg/kg compared with placebo, served as the basis for the approval of ipilimumab in the adjuvant setting. However, the subsequent intergroup trial, E1609 (described above), demonstrated better outcomes with low-dose (3 mg/kg) ipilimumab, which is also the dose approved for metastatic disease. </p>

4317</section>

4318</section>

4319</section>

4320<section id="_1112">

4321<h5 id="_1112_toc">

4322Combination signal transduction inhibitors</h5>

4323<section id="_1113">

4324<h6 id="_1113_toc">

4325Dabrafenib plus trametinib</h6>

4326<p id="_1114" tabindex="-1">

4327Evidence (dabrafenib plus trametinib):</p>

4328<div class="pdq-content-list">

4329<ol id="_1115">

4330<li>

4331 In a multinational, randomized, double-blind trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01682083">

4332COMBI-AD</a>

4333 [NCT01682083]), patients with stage IIIA, IIIB, or IIIC melanoma with <em class="gene-name">

4334BRAF</em>

4335 V600E or V600K mutations who underwent completion lymphadenectomy were randomly assigned (1:1) to receive either dabrafenib plus trametinib or two matched placebo tablets.[<a href="#cit/section_8.22">

433622</a>

4337][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4338Level of evidence B1</a>

4339] The primary end point of RFS was defined as time from randomization until the date of first recurrence or death from any cause. Patients with resection occurring more than 12 weeks before random assignment and an ECOG PS score of greater than 1 were excluded. Dabrafenib was given at a dose of 150 mg twice daily plus trametinib at a dose of 2 mg once daily (combination therapy) for 12 months in the absence of disease recurrence, unacceptable toxic effects, or death. A total of 870 patients were randomly assigned (438 patients to combination therapy and 432 patients to placebo). Baseline characteristics were balanced. Most patients (91%) harbored the V600E mutation compared with 9% who harbored the V600K mutation. Most patients (92%) had an ECOG PS of 0.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4340<ul id="_1116">

4341<li>

4342 At the data cutoff date for the primary analysis, the minimum follow-up was 2.5 years (median, 2.8 years), and all patients had completed trial treatment. Disease recurrence was reported in 163 of 438 patients (37%) who received combination therapy and in 247 of 432 patients (57%) who received placebo (HR<sub>

4343relapse or death</sub>

4344, 0.47; 95% CI, 0.39&#8211;0.58; <em>

4345P</em>

4346 &lt; .001). Median RFS had not been reached in the combination arm (95% CI, 44.5&#8211;not reached) and was 16.6 months (95% CI, 12.7&#8211;22.1) in the placebo group. </li>

4347<li>

4348 In the combination therapy arm, 26% of the patients had an AE leading to the discontinuation of therapy, 38% of the patients required dose reduction, and 66% of the patients required dose interruption. In the placebo arm, 3% of the patients had an AE leading to discontinuation of therapy, 3% of the patients required dose reduction, and 15% of the patients required dose interruption. Serious AEs occurred in 36% of the patients who received the combination therapy and 10% of the patients in the placebo group. One death, which resulted from pneumonia, was reported in the combination therapy arm. </li>

4349<li>

4350 An updated analysis performed at 5 years, after a minimum duration of 59 months of follow-up, showed superior RFS for patients who received the dabrafenib plus trametinib combination compared with patients who received placebo, with 52% (95% CI, 48%&#8211;58%) of patients who received the dabrafenib plus trametinib combination alive without relapse versus 36% (95% CI, 32%&#8211;41%) of patients who received placebo alive without relapse (HR<sub>

4351relapse or death</sub>

4352, 0.51; 95% CI, 0.42&#8211;0.61). Data are not mature for OS.[<a href="#cit/section_8.27">

435327</a>

4354] </li>

4355</ul>

4356</div>

4357</li>

4358</ol>

4359</div>

4360</section>

4361</section>

4362</section>

4363</section>

4364<section id="_426">

4365<h3 id="_426_toc">

4366Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation for Resectable Stage III Melanoma</h3>

4367<p id="_427" tabindex="-1">

4368Treatment options under clinical evaluation for patients with resectable stage III melanoma include the following:</p>

4369<div class="pdq-content-list">

4370<ol id="_428">

4371<li>

4372Trials of combination immunotherapies, including vaccines.</li>

4373<li>

4374Trials of adjuvant therapies that target a known mutation, e.g., <em class="gene-name">

4375c-KIT</em>

4376.</li>

4377<li>

4378Intralesional therapies.</li>

4379</ol>

4380</div>

4381</section>

4483<li id="section_8.23">

4484Maio M, Lewis K, Demidov L, et al.: Adjuvant vemurafenib in resected, BRAFV600 mutation-positive melanoma (BRIM8): a randomised, double-blind, placebo-controlled, multicentre, phase 3 trial. Lancet Oncol 21 (11): 1465-1477, 2020.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=32961119&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=32961119&amp;dopt=Abstract">

Lancet Oncol 22 (5): 643-654, 2021.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=33857412&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=33857412&amp;dopt=Abstract">

4556<section id="_672">

4557<h3 id="_672_toc">

4558Treatment Options for Unresectable Stage III, Stage IV, and Recurrent Melanoma</h3>

4559<p id="_832" tabindex="-1">

4560Treatment options for unresectable stage III, stage IV, and recurrent melanoma include the following:</p>

4561<div class="pdq-content-list">

4562<ol id="_833">

4563<li>

4564<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1026">

4565Intralesional therapy</a>
