4566.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4567<ol id="_1176" class="lower-alpha">

4568<li>

4569<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1027">

4570Talimogene laherparepvec (T-VEC)</a>

4571.</li>

4572</ol>

4573</div>

4574</li>

4575<li>

4576<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_681">

4577 Immunotherapy</a>

4578.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4579<ol id="_834" class="lower-alpha">

4580<li>

4581<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_682">

4582Checkpoint inhibitors</a>

4583.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4584<ul id="_1198">

4585<li>

4586<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_896">

4587Anti&#8211;programmed cell death-1 (PD-1) and programmed death-ligand 1 (PD-L1)</a>

4588.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4589<ul id="_1199" class="list-dash">

4590<li>

4591<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_935">

4592Pembrolizumab</a>

4593.</li>

4594<li>

4595<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_964">

4596Nivolumab</a>

4597.</li>

4598</ul>

4599</div>

4600</li>

4601<li>

4602<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1060">

4603Anti&#8211;cytotoxic T-lymphocyte antigen-4 (CTLA-4)</a>

4604.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4605<ul id="_1200" class="list-dash">

4606<li>

4607<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1061">

4608Ipilimumab</a>

4609.</li>

4610</ul>

4611</div>

4612</li>

4613</ul>

4614</div>

4615</li>

4616<li>

4617<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_693">

4618 High-dose interleukin-2 (IL-2)</a>

4619.</li>

4620<li>

4621<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_801">

4622Dual checkpoint inhibition</a>

4623.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4624<ul id="_1180">

4625<li>

4626<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1070">

4627CTLA-4 inhibitor plus PD-1 inhibitor</a>

4628.</li>

4629</ul>

4630</div>

4631</li>

4632</ol>

4633</div>

4634</li>

4635<li>

4636<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_699">

4637Signal transduction inhibitors</a>

4638.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4639<ol id="_836" class="lower-alpha">

4640<li>

4641<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_701">

4642 BRAF inhibitors</a>

4643 (for patients who test positive for the <em class="gene-name">

4644BRAF</em>

4645 V600 mutation).<div class="pdq-content-list">

4646<ul id="_837">

4647<li>

4648 <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_702">

4649Vemurafenib</a>

4650.</li>

4651<li>

4652<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_710">

4653 Dabrafenib</a>

4654.</li>

4655</ul>

4656</div>

4657</li>

4658<li>

4659<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_715">

4660Mitogen-activated protein kinase (MEK) inhibitors</a>

4661.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4662<ul id="_838">

4663<li>

4664<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_716">

4665 Trametinib</a>

4666.</li>

4667<li>

4668<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_956">

4669Cobimetinib</a>

4670.</li>

4671</ul>

4672</div>

4673</li>

4674<li>

4675<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1076">

4676KIT inhibitors</a>

4677.</li>

4678<li>

4679<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_721">

4680Combination therapy with signal transduction inhibitors</a>

4681.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4682<ul id="_839">

4683<li>

4684<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_945">

4685BRAF inhibitor plus MEK inhibitors</a>

4686.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4687<ul id="_974" class="list-dash">

4688<li>

4689<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1183">

4690Dabrafenib plus trametinib</a>

4691.</li>

4692<li>

4693<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1188">

4694Vemurafenib plus cobimetinib</a>

4695.</li>

4696<li>

4697<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1192">

4698Encorafenib plus binimetinib</a>

4699.</li>

4700</ul>

4701</div>

4702</li>

4703</ul>

4704</div>

4705 </li>

4706<li>

4707<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1298">

4708Combination signal transduction inhibitor therapy plus PD-L1 inhibitor</a>

4709.</li>

4710</ol>

4711</div>

4712</li>

4713<li>

4714<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_841">

4715Chemotherapy</a>

4716.</li>

4717<li>

4718<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_851">

4719Palliative local therapy</a>

4720.</li>

4721</ol>

4722</div>

4723<p id="_840" tabindex="-1">

4724Two approaches&#8212;checkpoint inhibition and targeting the mitogen-activated protein kinase (MAPK) pathway&#8212;demonstrated improvement in progression-free survival (PFS) and overall survival (OS) in randomized trials. Anti&#8211;PD-1 monotherapy (pembrolizumab or nivolumab) demonstrated improved efficacy outcomes with better safety profiles when compared with treatment using single-agent anti&#8211;CTLA-4 (ipilimumab) or investigator choice of chemotherapy. The combination of anti&#8211;PD-1 and anti&#8211;CTLA-4 immunotherapies (nivolumab and ipilimumab) also prolongs PFS and OS compared with ipilimumab, but the combination is associated with significant toxicity. The efficacy seen with immunotherapy is independent of <em class="gene-name">

4725BRAF</em>

4726 mutation status.</p>

4727<p id="_1297" tabindex="-1">

4728Combinations of BRAF and MEK inhibitors have consistently shown superior efficacy compared with BRAF monotherapy. Improved PFS was seen when a PD-L1 inhibitor (atezolizumab) was added to the combination of a BRAF plus MEK inhibitor (vemurafenib plus cobimetinib); however, data on OS is immature. Further questions remain regarding triplet therapy, including how it compares with monotherapy checkpoint inhibition and if the concurrent administration is superior to sequential therapy (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02224781">

4729NCT02224781</a>

4730).</p>

4731<p id="_1146" tabindex="-1">

4732Because of the rapid development of new agents, combinations, and remaining questions, patients and their physicians are encouraged to consider a clinical trial for initial treatment and at the time of progression. Clinical trials are addressing the following issues:</p>

4733<div class="pdq-content-list">

4734<ul id="_1159">

4735<li>

4736The value of sequencing therapies, such as immunotherapy and targeted therapy.</li>

4737<li>

4738Optimal doses for combination immunotherapy to decrease toxicity and preserve efficacy.</li>

4739<li>

4740 How to select the patients who will benefit from combination immunotherapy versus monotherapy.</li>

4741<li>

4742The role of PD-L1 expression as a biomarker for efficacy.</li>

4743<li>

4744The role of maintenance therapy.</li>

4745</ul>

4746</div>

4747<section id="_1026">

4748<h4 id="_1026_toc">

4749Intralesional therapy</h4>

4750<section id="_1027">

4751<h5 id="_1027_toc">

4752Talimogene laherparepvec (T-VEC)</h5>

4753<p id="_1028" tabindex="-1">

4754T-VEC is a genetically modified, herpes simplex virus type 1 (HSV1) oncolytic therapy approved for local intralesional injection into unresectable cutaneous, subcutaneous, and nodal lesions in patients with melanoma that recurs after initial surgery. T-VEC is designed to replicate within tumors, causing lysis, and to produce granulocyte-macrophage colony-stimulating factor (GM-CSF). Release of antigens together with virally derived GM-CSF may promote an antitumor immune response; however, the exact mechanism of action is unknown. </p>

4755<p id="_1029" tabindex="-1">

4756The approval of T-VEC by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) is based on data that demonstrated shrinkage of lesions. However, improvement of OS or an effect on visceral metastases or improvement in quality of life has not been shown. </p>

4757<p id="_1030" tabindex="-1">

4758Evidence (T-VEC):</p>

4759<div class="pdq-content-list">

4760<ol id="_1038">

4761<li>

4762In a multinational, randomized, open-label trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00769704">

4763NCT00769704</a>

4764), 436 patients were randomly assigned 2:1 to intralesional T-VEC or subcutaneous GM-CSF for at least 6 months or until there were no more injectable lesions.[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

47651</a>

4766][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4767Level of evidence B3</a>

4768] Eligible patients had stage IIIB, IIIC, and IV melanoma with unresectable, bidimensionally measurable lesions. The primary end point was durable response rate (DRR) (complete response [CR] or partial response [PR] lasting for &gt;6 months) as assessed by independent review. The study was stratified by site of first recurrence, presence of liver metastases, disease stage, and previous nonadjuvant systemic treatment. <div class="pdq-content-list">

4769<ul id="_1039">

4770<li>

4771The median patient age was 63 years (range 22&#8211;94 years), 70% of patients had a baseline Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group (ECOG) Performance Status (PS) score of 0, 30% had stage III disease, and 70% had stage IV disease (27% M1a; 21% M1b; and 22% M1c). Previous therapy for melanoma had been received by 53% of the patients. </li>

4772<li>

4773The first dose only was administered at 106 plaque-forming units (pfu)/mL to a maximum of 4 mL for all lesions combined. Subsequent doses were administered at 8 pfu/mL up to 4.0 mL for all injected lesions combined with the injected volume based on the size of the lesion. Injection into visceral lesions was not allowed. </li>

4774<li>

4775In patients treated with T-VEC, 16% (95% confidence interval [CI], 12.0%&#8211;20.5%) had a DRR versus 2% (95% CI, 0%&#8211;4.5%) in patients who received GM-CSF. Subgroup analysis suggests that the differences in DRRs between T-VEC versus GM-CSF may be greater in earlier-stage disease and treatment-na&#239;ve disease. Patients with stage IIIB and IIIC had a 33% DRR with T-VEC versus 0% with GM-CSF; 16% versus 2%, respectively in patients with stage IV M1a disease; 3% versus 4%, respectively in patients with stage IV M1b disease; and, 8% versus 3%, respectively in patients with stage IV M1c disease. Patients treated with T-VEC or GM-CSF as first-line therapy had a DRR of 24% versus 0%; however, patients who received treatment as second-line therapy or greater had a DRR of 10% versus 4%.</li>

4776<li>

4777The median duration of exposure to T-VEC was 23 weeks (5.3 months) with 26 patients exposed for more than 1 year. The most common adverse events (AEs) in the T-VEC group were fatigue (50%), chills (49%), pyrexia (43%), nausea (36%), influenza-like illness (30%), and injection site pain. The rate of discontinuation resulting from toxicity to T-VEC was 4% versus 2% in the GM-CSF group. Of the ten deaths in patients treated with T-VEC, eight deaths were considered the result of PD-1, salmonella infection, and one myocardial infarction; none were considered related to therapy, based on findings of the investigator.</li>

4778</ul>

4779</div>

4780</li>

4781</ol>

4782</div>

4783<p id="_1036" tabindex="-1">

4784<strong>

4785Precautions:</strong>

4786 T-VEC is a live, attenuated HSV and may cause life-threatening, disseminated herpetic infection. It is contraindicated in immunocompromised or pregnant patients. Healthcare providers and close contacts should avoid direct contact with injected lesions. Biohazard precautions for preparation, administration, and handling are provided in the label.</p>

4787<p id="_1037" tabindex="-1">

4788Detailed prescribing information by treatment cycle and lesion size are provided in the <a href="https://www.fda.gov/downloads/BiologicsBloodVaccines/CellularGeneTherapyProducts/ApprovedProducts/UCM469575.pdf?et_cid=36896905&amp;et_rid=1013830964&amp;linkid=http%3a%2f%2fwww.fda.gov%2fdownloads%2fBiologicsBloodVaccines%2fCellularGeneTherapyProducts%2fApprovedProducts%2fUCM469575.pdf" title="https://www.fda.gov/downloads/BiologicsBloodVaccines/CellularGeneTherapyProducts/ApprovedProducts/UCM469575.pdf?et_cid=36896905&amp;et_rid=1013830964&amp;linkid=http%3a%2f%2fwww.fda.gov%2fdownloads%2fBiologicsBloodVaccines%2fCellularGeneTherapyProducts%2fApprovedProducts%2fUCM469575.pdf">

4789FDA label</a>

4790.</p>

4791</section>

4792</section>

4793<section id="_681">

4794<h4 id="_681_toc">

4795Immunotherapy</h4>

4796<section id="_682">

4797<h5 id="_682_toc">

4798Checkpoint inhibitors</h5>

4799<section id="_896">

4800<h6 id="_896_toc">

4801Anti&#8211;PD-1 and PD-L1</h6>

4802<p id="_897" tabindex="-1">

4803The PD-1 pathway is a key immunoinhibitory mediator of T-cell exhaustion. Blockade of this pathway can lead to T-cell activation, expansion, and enhanced effector functions. PD-1 has two ligands, PD-L1 and PD-L2. Two anti&#8211;PD-1 antibodies, pembrolizumab and nivolumab, were approved by the FDA on the basis of improved OS in randomized trials.</p>

4804<section id="_935">

4805<h6 id="_935_toc">

4806Pembrolizumab</h6>

4807<p id="_928" tabindex="-1">

4808Evidence (pembrolizumab):</p>

4809<div class="pdq-content-list">

4810<ol id="_929">

4811<li>

4812<strong>

4813Previously treated patients.</strong>

4814 A total of 173 patients with unresectable or metastatic melanoma with disease progression within 24 weeks of the last dose of ipilimumab and, if <em class="gene-name">

4815BRAF</em>

4816 V600 mutation&#8722;positive, previous treatment with a BRAF inhibitor, were randomly assigned to one of two doses of pembrolizumab&#8212;2 mg/kg or 10 mg/kg&#8212;every 3 weeks. The trial excluded patients with an autoimmune disease, a condition requiring immunosuppression, or a history of severe immune-related adverse events (irAEs) from treatment with ipilimumab.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4817<ul id="_930">

4818<li>

4819The median age was 61 years; 60% were male; 67% had an ECOG PS score of 0, and 33% had an ECOG PS of 1. Eighteen percent of patients had tumors that were <em class="gene-name">

4820BRAF</em>

4821 V600 mutation&#8722;positive, 39% had an elevated lactate dehydrogenase (LDH), 64% had M1c disease, 9% had brain metastases, and 72% had undergone two or more therapies for advanced disease. The primary outcome measure was overall response rate according to Response Evaluation Criteria In Solid Tumors (RECIST, version 1.1) criteria as assessed by blinded independent central review.[<a href="#cit/section_9.2">

48222</a>

4823][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4824Level of evidence B3</a>

4825]</li>

4826<li>

4827The overall response rate determined by independent central review was 26% (95% CI, -14&#8211;13; <em>

4828P</em>

4829 = .96) in the 2 mg/kg arm, consisting of one CR and 20 PRs in 81 patients. Median follow-up was 8 months, and all patients had a minimum of 6 months of follow-up. Among the 21 patients with an objective response, 18 had ongoing responses, ranging from 1.4+ months to 8.5+ months.</li>

4830<li>

4831Response rate in the 10 mg/kg arm was similar at 26%, consisting of 20 responses in 76 patients. Responses were seen in patients with and without <em class="gene-name">

4832BRAF</em>

4833 V600 mutations. </li>

4834<li>

4835The approved dose was 2 mg/kg administered as an intravenous (IV) infusion for 30 minutes every 3 weeks.</li>

4836</ul>

4837</div>

4838<p id="_931" tabindex="-1">

4839Pembrolizumab was discontinued because of AEs in 7% of the patients treated with 2 mg/kg, with 3% considered drug-related AEs by the investigators. The most common AEs in the 2 mg/kg versus 10 mg/kg arms were the following:</p>

4840<div class="pdq-content-list">

4841<ul id="_932">

4842<li>

4843Fatigue (33% vs. 37%). </li>

4844<li>

4845Pruritus (23% vs. 19%). </li>

4846<li>

4847Rash (18% vs. 18%). </li>

4848</ul>

4849</div>

4850<p id="_933" tabindex="-1">

4851Other common AEs included cough, nausea, decreased appetite, constipation, arthralgia, and diarrhea. The most frequent and serious AEs that occurred in more than 2% of a total of 411 patients treated with pembrolizumab included renal failure, dyspnea, pneumonia, and cellulitis. Additional clinically significant irAEs included pneumonitis, colitis, hypophysitis, hyperthyroidism, hypothyroidism, nephritis, and hepatitis. </p>

4852<p id="_990" tabindex="-1">

4853The <a href="http://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2014/125514lbl.pdf" title="http://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2014/125514lbl.pdf">

4854FDA label</a>

4855 provides recommendations for suspected irAEs, including withholding the drug and administering corticosteroids.</p>

4856</li>

4857<li>

4858<strong>

4859Previously untreated and treated patients.</strong>

4860 A multicenter, international trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01866319">

4861KEYNOTE 006</a>

4862 [NCT01866319]) randomly assigned 834 patients with metastatic melanoma in a 1:1:1 ratio to receive pembrolizumab (10 mg/kg IV every 2 weeks or every 3 weeks) or four cycles of ipilimumab (3 mg/kg every 3 weeks).[<a href="#cit/section_9.3">

48633</a>

4864] Patients were stratified by ECOG PS (0 vs. 1), line of therapy (first-line vs. second-line), and PD-L1 expression (positive vs. negative). The primary end points were PFS and OS.[<a href="#cit/section_9.3">

48653</a>

4866][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4867Level of evidence A1</a>

4868]<p id="_999" tabindex="-1">

4869Approximately 66% of patients had received no previous systemic therapy for advanced melanoma. <em class="gene-name">

4870BRAF</em>

4871 V600 mutations were present in 36% of patients and of these, approximately 50% had received previous BRAF inhibitor treatments. The study did not enroll patients with <em class="gene-name">

4872BRAF</em>

4873 V600 mutations with high LDH levels and symptomatic or rapidly progressive disease who had not received anti-<em class="gene-name">

4874BRAF</em>

4875 therapy, which could provide rapid clinical benefit. Approximately 80% of patients had PD-L1&#8211;positive tissue samples.</p>

4876<div class="pdq-content-list">

4877<ul id="_1000">

4878<li>

4879 The final protocol-specified analysis of OS was conducted at a median follow-up of 23 months. Median OS was not reached in either pembrolizumab group; however, OS was 16.0 months for the ipilimumab group (hazard ratio [HR], 0.68; 95% CI, 0.53&#8722;0.87 for pembrolizumab every 2 weeks vs. ipilimumab; <em>

4880P</em>

4881 = .0009 and 0.68; 95% CI, 0.53&#8722;0.86 for pembrolizumab every 3 weeks vs. ipilimumab; <em>

4882P</em>

4883 = .0008). Survival rate at 24 months was 55% in the groups who received pembrolizumab every 2 weeks and every 3 weeks compared with 43% in the ipilimumab group.[<a href="#cit/section_9.4">

48844</a>

4885]</li>

4886<li>

4887Benefit was seen across all subgroups except for patients with PD-L1&#8211;negative tumors. However, since this subset was small (18% of patients) and the CI was wide, no definitive conclusions could be drawn from this study.</li>

4888</ul>

4889</div>

4890</li>

4891</ol>

4892</div>

4893</section>

4894<section id="_964">

4895<h6 id="_964_toc">

4896Nivolumab</h6>

4897<p id="_966" tabindex="-1">

4898Evidence (nivolumab):</p>

4899<div class="pdq-content-list">

4900<ol id="_967">

4901<li>

4902<strong>

4903Previously treated patients.</strong>

4904 Accelerated approval was based on a planned noncomparative interim analysis of the first 120 patients who received nivolumab with at least 6 months' follow-up from a multicenter, open-label trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01721746">

4905CheckMate 037</a>

4906 [NCT01721746]) that randomly assigned patients (2:1) to nivolumab (3 mg/kg every 2 weeks) or the investigator&#8217;s choice of chemotherapy (either dacarbazine 1,000 mg/m<span class="sup">

49072</span>

4908 IV every 3 weeks or the combination of carboplatin [area under the curve 6] every 3 weeks plus paclitaxel 175 mg/m<span class="sup">

49092</span>

4910 every 3 weeks).<a href="http://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2014/125554lbl.pdf" title="http://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2014/125554lbl.pdf">

4911[FDA label</a>

4912][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4913Level of evidence C3</a>

4914] Patients were required to have unresectable or metastatic melanoma that had progressed after treatment with ipilimumab and, if <em class="gene-name">

4915BRAF</em>

4916 V600 mutation&#8722;positive, a BRAF inhibitor. The trial excluded patients with an autoimmune disease, a condition requiring immunosuppression, or a history of severe irAEs from treatment with ipilimumab.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4917<ul id="_968">

4918<li>

4919 Median age of patients was 58 years; 65% of patients were male; and, ECOG PS was 0 in 58% of patients. <em class="gene-name">

4920BRAF</em>

4921 V600 mutation was present in 22% of patients; 76% had M1c disease; 56% had an elevated LDH; 18% had a history of brain metastases; and, 68% had received two or more systemic therapies previously for metastatic disease.</li>

4922<li>

4923Objective response rate and OS were coprimary end points. The objective response rate was 32% (95% CI, 23%&#8211;41%) with four CRs and 34 PRs as assessed by RECIST 1.1 criteria and an independent central review. Among the 38 patients with responses, 33 (87%) had ongoing responses with durations from 2.6+ to 10.0+ months.</li>

4924<li>

4925 Responses were seen in patients with and without <em class="gene-name">

4926BRAF</em>

4927 V600 mutations.</li>

4928<li>

4929 Safety analysis is based on 268 patients. Nivolumab was discontinued because of AEs in 9% of patients. Serious AEs occurred in 41% of patients and grade 3 and grade 4 AEs occurred in 42% of patients. The most common AEs were rash, cough, upper respiratory tract infection, and peripheral edema. Other important AEs included ventricular arrhythmia, iridocyclitis, increased amylase and lipase, dizziness, and neuropathy. </li>

4930</ul>

4931</div>

4932<p id="_969" tabindex="-1">

4933The FDA label provides recommendations for suspected irAEs, including withholding the drug and administering corticosteroids.</p>

4934</li>

4935<li>

4936<strong>

4937Previously untreated patients.</strong>

4938 A total of 418 patients with unresectable stage III or stage IV melanoma without a <em class="gene-name">

4939BRAF</em>

4940 mutation were randomly assigned (1:1) in a double-blind multicenter trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01721772">

4941CheckMate 066</a>

4942 [NCT01721772]) to receive nivolumab (3 mg/kg every 2 weeks) and a dacarbazine-matched placebo (every 3 weeks) or dacarbazine (1,000 mg/m<span class="sup">

49432</span>

4944 every 3 weeks with a nivolumab-matched placebo every 2 weeks). The primary end point was OS.[<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

49455</a>

4946][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4947Level of evidence A1</a>

4948] The trial was conducted in 80 centers in Europe, Israel, Australia, Canada, and South America, which are countries where dacarbazine had been a standard first-line treatment in patients without a <em class="gene-name">

4949BRAF</em>

4950 mutation.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4951<ul id="_970">

4952<li>

4953 The Data and Monitoring Safety Board (DMSB) noted a potential difference in OS during safety review. On June 10, 2014, an abbreviated report from an unplanned interim&#8211;database lock was reviewed showing a significant difference in OS in favor of nivolumab. The DMSB recommended that the study be unblinded and allow patients on dacarbazine to receive nivolumab. The intended sample size was approximately 410 patients; a total of 418 patients had been entered.</li>

4954<li>

4955 Results from the double-blind portion of the study before the crossover amendment showed that median OS was not reached in the nivolumab group and was 10.8 months (95% CI, 9.3&#8211;12.1) in the dacarbazine group. The OS rate at 1 year was 72.9% (95% CI, 65.%&#8211;78.9%) in the nivolumab group and 42.1% (95% CI, 33.0%&#8211;50.9%) in the dacarbazine group. The HR<sub>

4956death</sub>

4957 was 0.42; 99.79% CI, 0.25&#8211;0.73; <em>

4958P</em>

4959 &lt; .001.</li>

4960<li>

4961 The most common AEs in the nivolumab group were fatigue (19.9%), pruritus (17%), nausea (16.5%), and diarrhea (16%). In the nivolumab group, 6.8% of patients discontinued study treatment because of AEs compared with 11.7% of patients discontinuing study treatment in the dacarbazine group. AEs with potential immunological etiology that occurred included gastrointestinal, hepatic, pulmonary, renal, endocrine, and skin; however, the majority resolved with a delay in study treatment, glucocorticoid administration, or both per management guidelines for nivolumab. No deaths were attributed to drug-related AEs in either group. </li>

4962</ul>

4963</div>

4964</li>

4965<li>

4966<strong>

4967Change in dosing regimen for nivolumab in metastatic melanoma.</strong>

4968 <div class="pdq-content-list">

4969<ul id="_1117">

4970<li>

4971 In a population pharmacokinetic response analysis and a dose/exposure-response analysis, the flat dose of 240 mg of nivolumab every 2 weeks was considered pharmacokinetically equivalent to the dosing regimen of 3 mg/kg. Clinical safety and efficacy at the two doses appeared similar across body weight and tumor types in melanoma, non-small cell lung cancer, and renal cell carcinoma.[<a href="#cit/section_9.6">

49726</a>

4973]</li>

4974<li>

4975 The dosing regimen approved by the FDA for monotherapy has changed from 3 mg/kg to 240 mg IV every 2 weeks until disease progression or intolerable toxicity. The dosing regimen of 1 mg/kg of IV nivolumab when combined with ipilimumab will remain unchanged until after therapy with ipilimumab is complete, when the regimen will change to a 240 mg dose every 2 weeks until disease progression or intolerable toxicity.</li>

4976</ul>

4977</div>

4978</li>

4979</ol>

4980</div>

4981</section>

4982</section>

4983<section id="_1060">

4984<h6 id="_1060_toc">

4985Anti&#8211;cytotoxic T-lymphocyte antigen-4 (CTLA-4)</h6>

4986<section id="_1061">

4987<h6 id="_1061_toc">

4988Ipilimumab</h6>

4989<p id="_1062" tabindex="-1">

4990Ipilimumab is a human monoclonal antibody that binds to CTLA-4, thereby blocking its ability to downregulate T-cell activation, proliferation, and effector function.</p>

4991<p id="_1063" tabindex="-1">

4992Approved by the FDA in 2011, ipilimumab has demonstrated clinical benefit by prolonging OS in randomized trials. Two prospective, randomized, international trials, one each in previously untreated and treated patients, supported the use of ipilimumab.[<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

49937</a>

4994,<a href="#cit/section_9.8">

49958</a>

4996]</p>

4997<p id="_1064" tabindex="-1">

4998Evidence (ipilimumab):</p>

4999<div class="pdq-content-list">

5000<ol id="_1065">

5001<li>

5002<strong>

5003 Previously treated patients:</strong>

5004 A total of 676 patients with previously treated, unresectable stage III or stage IV disease, and who were HLA-A*0201-positive, entered into a three-arm, multinational, randomized (3:1:1), double-blind, double-placebo trial. A total of 403 patients were randomly assigned to receive ipilimumab (3 mg/kg every 3 weeks for 4 doses) with glycoprotein 100 (gp100) peptide vaccine. One hundred thirty-seven patients received ipilimumab (3 mg/kg every 3 weeks for 4 doses), and 136 patients received the gp100 vaccine. Patients were stratified by baseline metastases and previous receipt or nonreceipt of IL-2 therapy. Eighty-two of the patients had metastases to the brain at baseline.[<a href="#cit/section_9.8">

50058</a>

5006][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5007Level of evidence A1</a>

5008]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5009<ul id="_1066">

5010<li>

5011 The median OS was 10 months among patients who received ipilimumab alone and 10.1 months among those who received ipilimumab with the gp100 vaccine, compared with 6.4 months for patients who received the vaccine alone (HR of ipilimumab alone vs. gp100 alone, 0.66; <em>

5012P</em>

5013 &lt; .003; HR of ipilimumab plus vaccine vs. gp100 alone, 0.68; <em>

5014P</em>

5015 &lt; .001).</li>

5016<li>

5017 An analysis at 1 year showed that among patients treated with ipilimumab, 44% of those treated with ipilimumab and 45% of those treated with ipilimumab and the vaccine were alive, compared with 25% of the patients who received the vaccine only.</li>

5018<li>

5019 Grade 3 or grade 4 irAEs occurred in 10% to 15% of patients treated with ipilimumab. These irAEs most often included diarrhea or colitis, and endocrine-related events (e.g., inflammation of the pituitary). These events required cessation of therapy and institution of anti-inflammatory agents such as corticosteroids or, in four cases, infliximab (an antitumor necrosis factor-alpha antibody). </li>

5020<li>

5021 There were 14 drug-related deaths (2.1%), and seven deaths were associated with irAEs.</li>

5022</ul>

5023</div>

5024 </li>

5025<li>

5026<strong>

5027 Previously untreated patients:</strong>

5028 A multicenter, international trial randomly assigned 502 patients untreated for metastatic disease (adjuvant treatment was allowed) in a 1:1 ratio to receive ipilimumab (10 mg/kg) plus dacarbazine (850 mg/m<span class="sup">

50292</span>

5030) or placebo plus dacarbazine (850 mg/m<span class="sup">

50312</span>

5032) at weeks 1, 4, 7, and 10 followed by dacarbazine alone every 3 weeks through week 22. Patients with stable disease or an objective response and no dose-limiting toxic effects received ipilimumab or placebo every 12 weeks thereafter as maintenance therapy. The primary end point was survival. Patients were stratified according to ECOG PS and metastatic stage. Approximately 70% of the patients had an ECOG PS of 0, and the remainder of the patients had an ECOG PS of 1. Approximately 55% of patients had stage M1c disease.[<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

50337</a>

5034][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5035Level of evidence A1</a>

5036]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5037<ul id="_1067">

5038<li>

5039 The median OS was 11.2 months (95% CI, 9.4&#8211;13.6) for the ipilimumab-dacarbazine group versus 9.1 months (95% CI, 7.8&#8211;10.5) for the placebo-dacarbazine group. Estimated survival rates in the ipilimumab-dacarbazine group were 47.3% at 1 year, 28.5% at 2 years, and 20.8% at 3 years (HR<sub>

5040death</sub>

5041, 0.72; <em>

5042P </em>

5043&lt; .001); and in the placebo-dacarbazine group, the rates were 36.3% at 1 year, 17.9% at 2 years, and 12.2% at 3 years.</li>

5044<li>

5045 The most common study-drug&#8211;related AEs were those classified as immune related. Grade 3 or grade 4 irAEs were seen in 38.1% of patients treated with ipilimumab plus dacarbazine versus 4.4% of patients treated with placebo plus dacarbazine, the most common events were hepatitis and enterocolitis.</li>

5046<li>

5047 No drug-related deaths occurred.</li>

5048</ul>

5049</div>

5050</li>

5051</ol>

5052</div>

5053<p id="_1068" tabindex="-1">

5054Clinicians and patients should be aware that immune-mediated adverse reactions may be severe or fatal. Early identification and treatment are necessary, including potential administration of systemic glucocorticoids or other immunosuppressants according to the immune-mediated adverse reaction management guide provided by the manufacturer.[<a href="#cit/section_9.9">

50559</a>

5056]</p>

5057</section>

5058</section>

5059</section>

5060<section id="_693">

5061<h5 id="_693_toc">

5062High-dose IL-2</h5>

5063<p id="_694" tabindex="-1">

5064IL-2 was approved by the FDA in 1998 because of durable CRs in eight phase I and II studies. Phase III trials comparing high-dose IL-2 to other re-treatments, providing an assessment of relative impact on OS, have not been conducted. </p>

5065<p id="_696" tabindex="-1">

5066Evidence (high-dose IL-2):</p>

5067<div class="pdq-content-list">

5068<ol id="_791">

5069<li>

5070Based on a pooled analysis of 270 patients from eight single- and multi-institutional trials in 22 institutions conducted between 1985 and 1993:<div class="pdq-content-list">

5071<ul id="_792">

5072<li>

5073 High-dose IL-2 demonstrated a 6% to 7% CR rate.[<a href="#cit/section_9.10">

507410</a>

5075] </li>

5076<li>

5077With a median follow-up time for surviving patients of at least 7 years, the median duration of CRs was not reached but was at least 59 months.[<a href="#cit/section_9.11">

507811</a>

5079] </li>

5080</ul>

5081</div>

5082</li>

5083</ol>

5084</div>

5085<p id="_793" tabindex="-1">

5086Strategies to improve this therapy are an active area of investigation.</p>

5087</section>

5088<section id="_801">

5089<h5 id="_801_toc">

5090Dual checkpoint inhibition</h5>

5091<p id="_802" tabindex="-1">

5092

5093T-cells coexpress several receptors that inhibit T-cell function. Preclinical data and early clinical data suggest that co-blockade of the two inhibitory receptors, CTLA-4 and PD-1, may be more effective than blockade of either alone.[<a href="#cit/section_9.12">

509412</a>

5095] This has led to a phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01844505">

5096NCT01844505</a>

5097) comparing each single agent with the combination.

5098</p>

5099<section id="_1070">

5100<h6 id="_1070_toc">

5101CTLA-4 inhibitor plus PD-1 inhibitor</h6>

5102<p id="_1071" tabindex="-1">

5103Evidence (ipilimumab plus nivolumab):</p>

5104<div class="pdq-content-list">

5105<ol id="_1072">

5106<li>

5107<strong>

5108Previously untreated patients.</strong>

5109 In an international, randomized, double-blind trial (CheckMate 067), 945 previously untreated patients with unresectable stage III or IV melanoma were randomly assigned in a 1:1:1 ratio to receive the following:<div class="pdq-content-list">

5110<ul id="_1073">

5111<li>

5112Arm 1: nivolumab alone 3 mg/kg every 2 weeks plus placebo; </li>

5113<li>

5114Arm 2: nivolumab (1 mg/kg every 3 weeks) plus ipilimumab (3 mg/kg every 3 weeks for 4 doses) followed by 3 mg of nivolumab every 2 weeks; or </li>

5115<li>

5116Arm 3: ipilimumab alone (3 mg/kg every 3 weeks for 4 doses plus placebo).</li>

5117</ul>

5118</div>

5119<p id="_1074" tabindex="-1">

5120PFS and OS were coprimary end points. The study was powered to compare the combination of nivolumab plus ipilimumab with ipilimumab monotherapy, and nivolumab monotherapy with ipilimumab monotherapy; the study was not powered to compare combination ipilimumab plus nivolumab with nivolumab. </p>

5121<p id="_1147" tabindex="-1">

5122Patients were stratified according to tumor PD-L1 status assessed in a central laboratory by immunohistochemical testing (positive vs. negative or indeterminate), <em class="gene-name">

5123BRAF</em>

5124 mutation status (V600 mutation&#8722;positive vs. wild-type), and American Joint Committee on Cancer stage.[<a href="#cit/section_9.13">

512513</a>

5126][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5127Level of evidence A1</a>

5128]</p>

5129<div class="pdq-content-list">

5130<ol id="_1165" class="lower-alpha">

5131<li>

5132Characteristics at baseline included 74% of patients with an ECOG PS of 0; 36% had elevated LDH; 31.5% had a <em class="gene-name">

5133BRAF</em>

5134 mutation; and 58% had M1c disease. A minority of patients (23.6%) had a PD-L1&#8211;positive tumor.</li>

5135<li>

5136 The prospectively defined coprimary analysis of PFS occurred after all patients had at least 9 months of follow-up. Treatment with nivolumab alone or in combination with ipilimumab resulted in significantly longer PFS than with ipilimumab alone. Results were consistent across the prespecified stratification factors. Median PFS was 6.9 months (95% CI, 4.3&#8211;9.5) with nivolumab, 11.5 months (95% CI, 8.9&#8211;16.7) with nivolumab plus ipilimumab, and 2.9 months (95% CI, 2.8&#8211;3.4) with ipilimumab.</li>

5137<li>

5138The prospectively specified coprimary analysis of OS was to occur at 28 months. With 467 deaths, the rate of OS at this time point was 59% in the nivolumab group, 64% in the combination group, and 45% in the ipilimumab group (HR<sub>

5139death</sub>

5140 for the combination vs. ipilimumab, 0.55 [98% CI, 0.42&#8211;0.72; <em>

5141P</em>

5142&lt; .001]; HR<sub>

5143death</sub>

5144 with nivolumab vs. ipilimumab 0.63 [98% CI, 0.48&#8211;0.81; <em>

5145P</em>

5146&lt; .001]).[<a href="#cit/section_9.14">

514714</a>

5148]</li>

5149<li>

5150 In a descriptive analysis with a minimum follow-up of 36 months, the following data were found:<div class="pdq-content-list">

5151<ul id="_1166">

5152<li>

5153 OS rates were 52% in the nivolumab group, 58% in patients treated with the combination, and 34% in the ipilimumab group. </li>

5154<li>

5155 The median OS was not reached in the combination arm (95% CI, 38.2 months&#8211;not reached). Median OS in the single-agent nivolumab and ipilimumab groups were 37.6 months (95% CI, 29.1&#8211;not reached) and 19.9 months (95% CI, 16.9&#8211;24.6), respectively. </li>

5156<li>

5157 The HR<sub>

5158death</sub>

5159 for the combination versus ipilimumab was 0.55 (99.5% CI, 0.45&#8211;0.69; <em>

5160P</em>

5161 &lt; .001); for nivolumab versus ipilimumab, the HR was 0.65 (99.5% CI, 0.53&#8211;0.80; <em>

5162P</em>

5163 &lt; .001). </li>

5164</ul>

5165</div>

5166</li>

5167<li>

5168AEs were highest in the combination arm and need to be monitored carefully. Grade 3 to 4 treatment-related AEs occurred in 16.3% of patients in the nivolumab group, 27.3% of patients in the ipilimumab group, and 55% of patients in the combination group. The most frequent reason for treatment discontinuation was disease progression in the two monotherapy arms&#8212;49% with nivolumab and 65% with ipilimumab. The most frequent reason for discontinuation in the combination group was toxicity (38%).</li>

5169<li>

5170 Four therapy-related deaths were reported, which were attributed to neutropenia (nivolumab group), colon perforation (ipilimumab group), liver necrosis, and autoimmune myocarditis (combination ipilimumab and nivolumab). </li>

5171<li>

5172 Analyses of PD-L1 expression level associated with OS at 3 years indicated that the level of expression alone is a poor predictive biomarker of OS.</li>

5173</ol>

5174</div>

5175</li>

5176<li>

5177<strong>

5178Melanoma metastatic to the brain.</strong>

5179 Patients with at least one measurable, nonirradiated brain metastasis were eligible for treatment with systemic dual immunotherapy in an open-label, multicenter phase II trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02320058">

5180CheckMate 204</a>

5181 [NCT02320058]).[<a href="#cit/section_9.15">

518215</a>

5183][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5184Level of evidence C3</a>

5185] Eligibility required no need for immediate intervention, an absence of neurological signs or symptoms, and no glucocorticoids within 14 days of study treatment. Patients may have received previous stereotactic radiosurgery or excision of up to three brain metastases. Positive PD-L1 expression was not required.<p id="_1246" tabindex="-1">

5186 Treatment consisted of nivolumab (1 mg/kg) plus ipilimumab (3 mg/kg) every 3 weeks for up to 4 doses, followed by nivolumab (3 mg/kg) every 2 weeks until progression or unacceptable toxicity. </p>

5187<p id="_1247" tabindex="-1">

5188 The primary end point was rate of intracranial clinical benefit assessed by the investigator per RECIST criteria and defined as the percentage of patients with CR, PR, or stable disease for at least 6 months. A total of 28 sites in the United States enrolled 101 patients, of whom 94 had a minimum follow-up of 6 months; the data on that population are reported below.</p>

5189<div class="pdq-content-list">

5190<ul id="_1248">

5191<li>

5192 Clinical benefit (in the brain) was seen in 57% of patients (95% CI, 47&#8211;68); 24 patients (26%) had a CR, 28 patients (30%) had a PR, and 2 patients (2%) had stable disease that lasted for 6 months or longer. Similar rates of objective response (50%) were seen in patients with extracranial lesions, although fewer patients had a CR (7%). </li>

5193<li>

5194A subgroup analysis indicated responses in both PD-L1&#8211;positive and PD-L1&#8211;negative patients (baseline status not known in 20/94 patients).</li>

5195<li>

5196The median follow-up of the 94 patients was 14 months. Median time to intracranial response was 2.3 months (range, 1.1&#8722;10.8), and time to extracranial response was 2.1 months (range, 1.1&#8722;15.0).</li>

5197<li>

5198The most common treatment-related AE of any grade in the nervous system was headache (21 patients [22%]), with 3 patients (3%) having headache of grade 3 or 4. Other treatment-related neurological AEs of grade 3 or 4 were brain edema (2 patients [2%]), intracranial hemorrhage (1 patient [1%]), peripheral motor neuropathy (1 patient [1%]), and syncope (1 patient [1%]). Each of these AEs led to treatment discontinuation, and the one reported case of peripheral motor neuropathy was irreversible. One death was evaluated by the investigator as related to the study treatment (grade 5 immune-related myocarditis).</li>

5199<li>

5200 Progression was documented in 33 patients (35%); 17 patients (18%) had intracranial progression only, 4 patients (4%) had extracranial progression only, and 12 patients (13%) had progression in both intracranial and extracranial sites.</li>

5201</ul>

5202</div>

5203</li>

5204</ol>

5205</div>

5206</section>

5207</section>

5208</section>

5209<section id="_699">

5210<h4 id="_699_toc">

5211Signal transduction inhibitors</h4>

5212<p id="_700" tabindex="-1">

5213Studies to date indicate that both BRAF and MEK (mitogen-activated ERK-[extracellular signal-regulated kinase] activating kinase) inhibitors, as single agents and in combination, can significantly impact the natural history of melanoma, although they do not appear to provide a cure.</p>

5214<section id="_701">

5215<h5 id="_701_toc">

5216BRAF inhibitors</h5>

5217<p id="_1249" tabindex="-1">

5218Treatment with BRAF inhibitors is discouraged in wild-type <em class="gene-name">

5219BRAF</em>

5220 melanoma because data from preclinical models have demonstrated that BRAF inhibitors can enhance rather than downregulate the mitogen-activated protein kinase (MAPK) pathway in tumor cells with wild-type <em class="gene-name">

5221BRAF</em>

5222 and upstream <em class="gene-name">

5223RAS</em>

5224 mutations.[<a href="#cit/section_9.16">

522516</a>

5226-<a href="#cit/section_9.19">

522719</a>

5228]</p>

5229<section id="_702">

5230<h6 id="_702_toc">

5231Vemurafenib</h6>

5232<p id="_703" tabindex="-1">

5233Vemurafenib is an orally available, small-molecule, selective BRAF kinase inhibitor that was approved by the FDA in 2011 for patients with unresectable or metastatic melanoma who test positive for the <em class="gene-name">

5234BRAF</em>

5235 V600E mutation. </p>

5236<p id="_706" tabindex="-1">

5237Evidence (vemurafenib):</p>

5238<div class="pdq-content-list">

5239<ol id="_707">

5240<li>

5241 <strong>

5242Previously untreated patients: </strong>

5243The approval of vemurafenib was supported by an international, multicenter trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01006980">

5244BRIM-3</a>

5245 [NCT01006980]) that screened 2,107 patients with previously untreated stage IIIC or IV melanoma for the <em class="gene-name">

5246BRAF</em>

5247 V600 mutation and identified 675 patients via the cobas 4800 <em class="gene-name">

5248BRAF</em>

5249 V600 Mutation Test.[<a href="#cit/section_9.20">

525020</a>

5251] Patients were randomly assigned to receive either vemurafenib (960 mg by mouth twice a day) or dacarbazine (1,000 mg/m<span class="sup">

52522</span>

5253 IV every 3 weeks). Coprimary end points were rates of OS and PFS. At the planned interim analysis, the DMSB determined that both the OS and PFS end points had met the prespecified criteria for statistical significance in favor of vemurafenib and recommended that patients in the dacarbazine group be allowed to cross over to receive vemurafenib.[<a href="#cit/section_9.20">

525420</a>

5255][Levels of evidence <a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5256A1</a>

5257 and <a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5258B1</a>

5259] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5260<ul id="_708">

5261<li>

5262 A total of 675 patients were evaluated for OS; although the median survival had not yet been reached for vemurafenib and the data were immature for reliable Kaplan-Meier estimates of survival curves, the OS in the vemurafenib arm was clearly superior to that in the dacarbazine arm.</li>

5263<li>

5264 The HR<sub>

5265death</sub>

5266 in the vemurafenib group was 0.37 (95% CI, 0.26&#8211;0.55; <em>

5267P</em>

5268 &lt; .001). The survival benefit in the vemurafenib group was observed in each prespecified subgroup, for example, age, sex, ECOG PS, tumor stage, LDH, and geographic region. </li>

5269<li>

5270 The HR for tumor progression in the vemurafenib arm was 0.26 (95% CI, 0.20&#8211;0.33; <em>

5271P</em>

5272 &lt; .001). The estimated median PFS was 5.3 months in the vemurafenib arm versus 1.6 months in the dacarbazine arm. </li>

5273<li>

5274 Twenty patients had non-<em class="gene-name">

5275BRAF</em>

5276 V600E mutations: 19 with <em class="gene-name">

5277BRAF</em>

5278 V600K and 1 with <em class="gene-name">

5279BRAF</em>

5280 V600D. Four patients with a <em class="gene-name">

5281BRAF</em>

5282 V600K mutation had a response to vemurafenib. </li>

5283<li>

5284 AEs required dose modification or interruption in 38% of patients who received vemurafenib and 16% of those who received dacarbazine. The most common AEs with vemurafenib were cutaneous events, arthralgia, and fatigue. Cutaneous squamous cell carcinoma (SCC), keratoacanthoma, or both developed in 18% of patients and were treated by simple excision. The most common AEs with dacarbazine were fatigue, nausea, vomiting, and neutropenia. For more information, see <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/fatigue/fatigue-hp-pdq">

5285Fatigue</a>

5286 and <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/nausea/nausea-hp-pdq">

5287Nausea and Vomiting Related to Cancer Treatment</a>

5288.</li>

5289</ul>

5290</div>

5291</li>

5292<li>

5293<strong>

5294Previously treated patients:</strong>

5295 A total of 132 patients with a <em class="gene-name">

5296BRAF</em>

5297 V600E or <em class="gene-name">

5298BRAF</em>

5299 V600K mutation were enrolled in a multicenter phase II trial of vemurafenib, which was administered as 960 mg by mouth twice a day. Of the enrolled patients, 61% had stage M1c disease, and 49% had an elevated LDH level. All patients had received one or more previous therapies for advanced disease. Median follow-up was 12.9 months.[<a href="#cit/section_9.21">

530021</a>

5301][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5302Level of evidence C3</a>

5303]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5304<ul id="_709">

5305<li>

5306 An independent review committee (IRC) reported a 53% response rate (95% CI, 44%&#8211;62%), with eight patients (6%) achieving CR.</li>

5307<li>

5308 Median duration of response per IRC assessment was 6.7 months (95% CI, 5.6&#8211;8.6). Most responses were evident at the first radiological assessment at 6 weeks; however, some patients did not respond until after receiving therapy for more than 6 months.</li>

5309</ul>

5310</div>

5311</li>

5312</ol>

5313</div>

5314</section>

5315<section id="_710">

5316<h6 id="_710_toc">

5317Dabrafenib</h6>

5318<p id="_711" tabindex="-1">

5319Dabrafenib is an orally available, small-molecule, selective BRAF inhibitor that was approved by the FDA in 2013. It is used for treatment of patients with unresectable or metastatic melanoma who test positive for the <em class="gene-name">

5320BRAF</em>

5321 V600E mutation as detected by an FDA-approved test. Dabrafenib and other BRAF inhibitors are not recommended for treatment of <em class="gene-name">

5322BRAF</em>

5323 wild-type melanomas, as <em>

5324in vitro</em>

5325 experiments suggest there may be a paradoxical stimulation of MAPK signaling resulting in tumor promotion.</p>

5326<p id="_712" tabindex="-1">

5327Evidence (dabrafenib):</p>

5328<div class="pdq-content-list">

5329<ol id="_713">

5330<li>

5331 An international, multicenter trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01227889">

5332BREAK-3</a>

5333 [NCT01227889]) compared dabrafenib with dacarbazine. A total of 250 patients with unresectable stage III or IV melanoma and <em class="gene-name">

5334BRAF</em>

5335 V600E mutations were randomly assigned in a 3:1 ratio (dabrafenib 150 mg by mouth every day or dacarbazine 1,000 mg/m<span class="sup">

53362</span>

5337 IV every 3 weeks). IL-2 was allowed as a previous treatment for advanced disease. The primary end point was PFS; patients could cross over at the time of progressive disease after confirmation by a blinded IRC.[<a href="#cit/section_9.22">

533822</a>

5339][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5340Level of evidence B1</a>

5341]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5342<ul id="_714">

5343<li>

5344 With 126 events, the HR for PFS was 0.30 (95% CI, 0.18&#8211;0.51; <em>

5345P</em>

5346 &lt; .0001). The estimated median PFS was 5.1 months for dabrafenib versus 2.7 months for dacarbazine. OS data are limited by the median duration of follow-up and crossover. The PR rate was 47% and the CR rate was 3% in patients who received dabrafenib versus a 5% PR rate and a 2% CR rate for those who received dacarbazine.</li>

5347<li>

5348 The most frequent AEs in patients treated with dabrafenib were cutaneous findings (i.e., hyperkeratosis, papillomas, palmar-plantar erythrodysesthesia), pyrexia, fatigue, headache, and arthralgia. Cutaneous SCC or keratoacanthoma occurred in 12 patients, basal cell carcinoma occurred in four patients, mycosis fungoides occurred in one patient, and new melanoma occurred in two patients.</li>

5349</ul>

5350</div>

5351</li>

5352</ol>

5353</div>

5354</section>

5355</section>

5356<section id="_715">

5357<h5 id="_715_toc">

5358MEK inhibitors</h5>

5359<section id="_716">

5360<h6 id="_716_toc">

5361Trametinib</h6>

5362<p id="_717" tabindex="-1">

5363Trametinib is an orally available, small-molecule, selective inhibitor of MEK1 and MEK2. <em class="gene-name">

5364BRAF</em>

5365 activates MEK1 and MEK2 proteins, which in turn, activate MAPK. Preclinical data suggest that MEK inhibitors can restrain growth and induce cell death of some <em class="gene-name">

5366BRAF</em>

5367-mutated human melanoma tumors. </p>

5368<p id="_794" tabindex="-1">

5369In 2013, trametinib was approved by the FDA for patients with unresectable or metastatic melanoma with <em class="gene-name">

5370BRAF</em>

5371 V600E or V600K mutations, as determined by an FDA-approved test. </p>

5372<p id="_718" tabindex="-1">

5373Evidence (trametinib):</p>

5374<div class="pdq-content-list">

5375<ol id="_719">

5376<li>

5377 A total of 1,022 patients were screened for <em class="gene-name">

5378BRAF</em>

5379 mutations, resulting in 322 eligible patients (281 with <em class="gene-name">

5380BRAF</em>

5381 V600E, 40 with <em class="gene-name">

5382BRAF</em>

5383 V600K, and one with both mutations).[<a href="#cit/section_9.23">

538423</a>

5385] One previous treatment (biological or chemotherapy) was allowed; however, no previous treatment with a BRAF or MEK inhibitor was permitted. Patients were randomly assigned in a 2:1 ratio to receive trametinib (2 mg every day) or IV chemotherapy (either dacarbazine 1,000 mg/m<span class="sup">

53862</span>

5387 every 3 weeks or paclitaxel 175 mg/m<span class="sup">

53882</span>

5389 every 3 weeks). Crossover for patients randomly assigned to chemotherapy was allowed; therefore, the primary end point was PFS. <div class="pdq-content-list">

5390<ul id="_720">

5391<li>

5392 The investigator-assessed PFS was 4.8 months in patients who received trametinib versus 1.5 months in the chemotherapy group (HR for PFS or death, 0.45; 95% CI, 0.33&#8211;0.63; <em>

5393P</em>

5394 &lt; .001). A radiology review blinded-to-treatment arm resulted in similar outcomes. Median OS has not been reached. </li>

5395<li>

5396AEs leading to dose interruptions occurred in 35% of patients in the trametinib group and 22% of those in the chemotherapy group. AEs leading to dose reductions occurred in 27% of patients who received trametinib and in 10% of those who received chemotherapy. </li>

5397<li>

5398 The most common AEs included rash, diarrhea, nausea, vomiting, fatigue, peripheral edema, alopecia, hypertension, and constipation. Cardiomyopathy (7%), interstitial lung disease (2.4%), central serous retinopathy (&lt;1%), and retinal-vein occlusion (&lt;1%) are uncommon but serious AEs associated with trametinib. On-study cutaneous SCCs were not observed. For more information, see <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/fatigue/fatigue-hp-pdq">

5399Fatigue</a>

5400 and <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/nausea/nausea-hp-pdq">

5401Nausea and Vomiting Related to Cancer Treatment</a>

5402.</li>

5403</ul>

5404</div>

5405</li>

5406</ol>

5407</div>

5408</section>

5409<section id="_956">

5410<h6 id="_956_toc">

5411Cobimetinib</h6>

5412<p id="_957" tabindex="-1">

5413Cobimetinib is a small-molecule, selective MEK inhibitor that the FDA approved in 2015 for use in combination with the BRAF inhibitor vemurafenib. For more information, see the <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_721">

5414Combination therapy with signal transduction inhibitors</a>

5415 section.</p>

5416</section>

5417</section>

5418<section id="_1076">

5419<h5 id="_1076_toc">

5420KIT inhibitors</h5>

5421<p id="_1077" tabindex="-1">

5422Early data suggest that mucosal or acral melanomas with activating mutations or amplifications in <em class="gene-name">

5423c-KIT</em>

5424 may be sensitive to a variety of c-KIT inhibitors.[<a href="#cit/section_9.24">

542524</a>

5426-<a href="#cit/section_9.26">

542726</a>

5428] Phase II and phase III trials are available for patients with unresectable stage III or stage IV melanoma harboring the <em class="gene-name">

5429c-KIT</em>

5430 mutation.</p>

5431</section>

5432<section id="_721">

5433<h5 id="_721_toc">

5434Combination therapy with signal transduction inhibitors</h5>

5435<p id="_1250" tabindex="-1">

5436Results from phase III trials comparing three different combinations of BRAF-MEK inhibitors with BRAF inhibitor monotherapy have consistently shown efficacy superior to BRAF monotherapy.</p>

5437<p id="_722" tabindex="-1">

5438Secondary resistance to BRAF inhibitor monotherapy in patients with <em class="gene-name">

5439BRAF</em>

5440 V600 mutations may be associated with reactivation of the MAPK pathway. Therefore, combinations of signal transduction inhibitors that block different sites in the same pathway or sites in multiple pathways are an active area of research. </p>

5441<section id="_945">

5442<h6 id="_945_toc">

5443BRAF inhibitor plus MEK inhibitors</h6>

5444<section id="_1183">

5445<h6 id="_1183_toc">

5446Dabrafenib plus trametinib</h6>

5447<p id="_1184" tabindex="-1">

5448Evidence (dabrafenib plus trametinib):</p>

5449<div class="pdq-content-list">

5450<ol id="_1185">

5451<li>

5452<strong>

5453Previously untreated.</strong>

5454 An international, double-blind, phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01584648">

5455COMBI-d</a>

5456 [NCT01584648]) without crossover randomly assigned 423 previously untreated patients with unresectable stage IIIC or stage IV melanoma with <em class="gene-name">

5457BRAF</em>

5458 V600E or V600K mutations to receive the combination of dabrafenib (150 mg by mouth twice a day) plus trametinib (2 mg by mouth every day) or dabrafenib plus placebo. The primary end point was investigator-assessed PFS. The protocol included a prespecified interim analysis for OS at the time of analysis of the primary end point. Patients were stratified by baseline LDH and <em class="gene-name">

5459BRAF</em>

5460 genotype.[<a href="#cit/section_9.27">

546127</a>

5462][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5463Level of evidence B1</a>

5464]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5465<ul id="_1186">

5466<li>

5467Median PFS was 9.3 months for the combination versus 8.8 months for dabrafenib plus placebo. The HR<sub>

5468death</sub>

5469 or progression was 0.75 (95% CI, 0.57&#8211;0.99; <em>

5470P</em>

5471 = .03). Updated data at the time of final analysis of OS revealed a median PFS of 11.0 months for the combination versus 8.8 months for dabrafenib plus placebo. The HR for PFS or death was 0.67 (95% CI, 0.53&#8211;0.84; <em>

5472P</em>

5473 = .0004; unadjusted for multiple testing).[<a href="#cit/section_9.28">

547428</a>

5475] </li>

5476<li>

5477 A prespecified final analysis of OS was conducted at 70% of events. Median OS was 25.1 months in the dabrafenib-plus-trametinib group (66% events) versus 18.7 months in the dabrafenib-plus-placebo group (76% events). The HR was 0.71 (95% CI, 0.55&#8211;0.92; <em>

5478P</em>

5479 = 0.01). </li>

5480<li>

5481 Permanent discontinuations of study drugs were reported in 9% of patients on the combination and in 5% of patients treated with dabrafenib only. </li>

5482<li>

5483 The incidence of grade 3 to grade 4 AEs was similar between the groups: a 35% incidence with the combination and a 37% incidence with dabrafenib only. Pyrexia occurred more frequently with the combination and was treated with immediate temporary cessation of the study drug in either group; prophylactic glucocorticoids may prevent recurring episodes. Hyperproliferative cutaneous events, including cutaneous SCCs, which were considered related to paradoxical activation of the MAPK pathway and occurred less frequently with the addition of the MEK inhibitor. Rare, but serious, AEs included decreased ejection fraction and chorioretinopathy.</li>

5484</ul>

5485</div>

5486</li>

5487<li>

5488<strong>

5489 Previously untreated.</strong>

5490 An international, open-label, phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01597908">

5491COMBI-v</a>

5492 [NCT01597908]) randomly assigned 704 previously untreated patients with metastatic melanoma with a <em class="gene-name">

5493BRAF</em>

5494 V600 mutation to receive standard doses of either the combination of dabrafenib plus trametinib or vemurafenib as first-line therapy. The primary end point was OS.[<a href="#cit/section_9.29">

549529</a>

5496][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5497Level of evidence A1</a>

5498]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5499<ul id="_1187">

5500<li>

5501 An interim analysis for OS was planned when 202 of the final 288 events occurred. Per protocol, the DMSB used adjusted efficacy boundaries for actual events (222) (2-sided <em>

5502P</em>

5503 &lt; .0214 for efficacy and <em>

5504P</em>

5505 &gt; .2210 for futility). The DMSB recommended stopping for efficacy, and the interim analysis is considered to be the final analysis of OS. A protocol amendment was issued to allow crossover to the combination therapy arm.</li>

5506<li>

5507A total of 100 patients (28%) in the combination arm and 122 (35%) in the vemurafenib group had died (HR, 0.69; 95% CI, 0.53&#8211;0.89; <em>

5508P</em>

5509 = .005). Median OS for patients treated with vemurafenib was 17.2 months; the median has not been reached in the combination therapy arm.</li>

5510</ul>

5511</div>

5512</li>

5513<li>

5514<strong>

5515Previously untreated.</strong>

5516 A pooled analysis of the 563 patients who were randomly assigned to receive dabrafenib plus trametinib in the COMBI-d (double-blinded) and COMBI-v (open label) trials (described above) provides estimated 5-year outcomes.[<a href="#cit/section_9.30">

551730</a>

5518] After the study, 53% of patients received subsequent treatment; two-thirds of these patients received immunotherapy. <div class="pdq-content-list">

5519<ul id="_1258">

5520<li>

5521Sixty-three percent of patients died (64% in COMBI-d and 61% in COMBI-v) after a median follow-up of 22 months (range, 0&#8722;76 months).</li>

5522<li>

5523The estimated 5-year OS rate was 34% (95% CI, 30%&#8722;38%) and the investigator-assessed PFS rate was 19% (95% CI, 15%&#8722;22%). </li>

5524<li>

5525A CR, which occurred in 109 patients (19%), was associated with an OS rate of 71% (95% CI, 62%&#8722;79%) at 5 years.

5526</li>

5527</ul>

5528</div>

5529</li>

5530</ol>

5531</div>

5532</section>

5533<section id="_1188">

5534<h6 id="_1188_toc">

5535Vemurafenib plus cobimetinib</h6>

5536<p id="_1189" tabindex="-1">

5537Evidence (vemurafenib plus cobimetinib):</p>

5538<div class="pdq-content-list">

5539<ol id="_1190">

5540<li>

5541<strong>

5542Previously untreated. </strong>

5543An international phase III trial randomly assigned 495 patients with previously untreated, unresectable stage IIIC or stage IV melanoma with <em class="gene-name">

5544BRAF</em>

5545 V600 mutation&#8722;positive melanoma to receive the combination of vemurafenib (960 mg by mouth every day) and cobimetinib (60 mg by mouth every day for 21 days followed by a 7-day rest period) or vemurafenib plus placebo. The primary end point was investigator-assessed PFS. Crossover at time of PFS was not allowed. Patients were stratified by stage and geographic region. Two interim analyses of OS were prespecified, with the first specified at the time of analysis of the primary end point.[<a href="#cit/section_9.31">

554631</a>

5547][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5548Level of evidence B1</a>

5549]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5550<ul id="_1191">

5551<li>

5552 Median PFS was 9.9 months for the combination versus 6.2 months in patients treated with vemurafenib plus placebo. The HR<sub>

5553progression or death</sub>

5554 was 0.51 (95% CI, 0.39&#8211;0.68; <em>

5555P</em>

5556 = .001).</li>

5557<li>

5558 The first interim analysis of OS is immature because of the few events in both arms; therefore, median survival was not reached in either study group.</li>

5559<li>

5560 Rate of withdrawal of therapy caused by AEs was similar between the groups: a 13% rate was found with patients treated with the combination, and a 12% rate was found with patients treated with vemurafenib only. Six deaths were attributed to AEs in the combination group, and three deaths were attributed to AEs in the vemurafenib-only group.</li>

5561<li>

5562 The incidence of grade 3 to grade 4 AEs was similar between the groups: a 62% incidence rate was found in patients treated with the combination, and a 58% rate was found in patients treated with vemurafenib alone. Rare, but serious, AEs included chorioretinopathy, retinal detachment, decreased ejection fraction, and QT prolongation. Hyperproliferative cutaneous events, including cutaneous SCC, were considered to be related to paradoxical activation of the MAPK pathway and occurred less frequently with the addition of the MEK inhibitor. </li>

5563</ul>

5564</div>

5565</li>

5566</ol>

5567</div>

5568</section>

5569<section id="_1192">

5570<h6 id="_1192_toc">

5571Encorafenib plus binimetinib</h6>

5572<p id="_1251" tabindex="-1">

5573

5574Encorafenib is a small-molecule BRAF inhibitor that is approved in combination with binimetinib, a small-molecule MEK inhibitor, for the treatment of unresectable or metastatic melanoma with a <em class="gene-name">

5575BRAF</em>

5576 V600E or V600K mutation, as detected by an FDA-approved test. The combination has demonstrated improved PFS and OS compared with vemurafenib; however, neither is approved as single-agent therapy.

5577</p>

5578<p id="_1193" tabindex="-1">

5579Evidence (encorafenib plus binimetinib):</p>

5580<div class="pdq-content-list">

5581<ol id="_1194">

5582<li>

5583<strong>

5584Previously untreated or progression on or after first-line immunotherapy.</strong>

5585 An international, open-label, phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01909453">

5586COLUMBUS</a>

5587 [NCT01909453]) randomly assigned 577 patients with stage IIIB, IIIC, or IV melanoma with <em class="gene-name">

5588BRAF</em>

5589 V600 mutation&#8211;positive melanoma in a 1:1:1 ratio to receive encorafenib (450 mg every day) plus binimetinib (45 mg twice a day) or encorafenib monotherapy (300 mg every day) or vemurafenib monotherapy (960 mg twice a day).[<a href="#cit/section_9.32">

559032</a>

5591,<a href="#cit/section_9.33">

559233</a>

5593] The primary end point was PFS for the combination versus vemurafenib as assessed by a blinded IRC with a secondary end point of OS.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5594<ul id="_1196">

5595<li>

5596A minority of patients (approximately 5%) had received previous checkpoint inhibitor therapy.

5597

5598</li>

5599<li>

5600 With a median follow-up of 16.6 months, median PFS was 14.9 months (95% CI, 11.0&#8211;18.5) with the combination versus 7.3 months (95% CI, 5.6&#8211;8.2) with vemurafenib. The HR<sub>

5601progression or death</sub>

5602 was 0.54 (95% CI, 0.41&#8211;0.71; 2-sided <em>

5603P</em>

5604 &lt; .0001).</li>

5605<li>

5606 With a median follow-up of 36.8 months for the secondary end point of OS, patients in the combination arm had a median OS of 33.6 months (95% CI, 24.4&#8211;39.2) versus 16.9 months (95% CI, 14.0&#8211;24.5) for patients treated with vemurafenib (HR, 0.61; 95% CI, 0.47&#8211;0.79; <em>

5607P</em>

5608 &lt; .0001). Subsequent treatments received after discontinuation of the study drug were received by 42% of patients in the combination group and 62% of patients in the vemurafenib group.[<a href="#cit/section_9.32">

560932</a>

5610,<a href="#cit/section_9.33">

561133</a>

5612][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5613Level of evidence A1</a>

5614]</li>

5615<li>

5616The incidence of grade 3 to 4 AEs was 58% with combination therapy and 63% with vemurafenib. Serious AEs occurred in 34% of the combination group and 37% of the vemurafenib group. The most common AEs in the combination group included gastrointestinal symptoms and elevation of gamma-glutamyl transferase (GGT), elevation of creatine phosphokinase (CPK), left ventricular dysfunction (8%) and serous retinopathy (20%), mostly grade 1 to 2 (monitoring guidelines are provided in the drug label). Patients who received vemurafenib had more pyrexia and cutaneous toxicities. Study drug discontinuations from AEs were 15% in the combination group and 17% with vemurafenib. No deaths were considered to be related to treatment; however, one death from suicide occurred in the combination arm. </li>

5617</ul>

5618</div>

5619</li>

5620</ol>

5621</div>

5622</section>

5623</section>

5624</section>

5625<section id="_1298">

5626<h5 id="_1298_toc">

5627 Combination signal transduction inhibitor therapy plus PD-L1 inhibitor</h5>

5628<section id="_1299">

5629<h6 id="_1299_toc">

5630Cobimetinib and vemurafenib plus atezolizumab</h6>

5631<p id="_1300" tabindex="-1">

5632Evidence (cobimetinib and vemurafenib plus atezolizumab):</p>

5633<div class="pdq-content-list">

5634<ol id="_1301">

5635<li>

5636A double-blind, placebo-controlled, multicenter trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02908672">

5637IMspire150</a>

5638 [NCT02908672]) randomly assigned (in a 1:1 ratio) 514 patients with <em class="gene-name">

5639BRAF</em>

5640 V600 mutation&#8722;positive unresectable stage IIIC or metastatic melanoma to receive first-line therapy with cobimetinib plus vemurafenib with either atezolizumab or placebo.[<a href="#cit/section_9.34">

564134</a>

5642] Eligibility criteria included ECOG PS scores of 0 to 1, measurable disease, and no previous systemic treatment for metastatic melanoma. Patients with untreated or actively progressing brain metastases or a history of serious autoimmune disease were excluded. Previous adjuvant therapy was allowed (14% of patients).<p id="_1302" tabindex="-1">

5643After all patients in both arms received a 28-day cycle of cobimetinib and vemurafenib, patients received atezolizumab (840 mg IV every 2 weeks) or placebo in addition to the combination BRAF-MEK inhibitor therapy. The primary efficacy end point was investigator-assessed PFS per RECIST 1.1 criteria. </p>

5644<div class="pdq-content-list">

5645<ul id="_1303">

5646<li>

5647 At a median follow-up of 19 months, the primary investigator median PFS was 15 months (95% CI, 11.4&#8722;18.4) in the atezolizumab arm and 11 months (95% CI, 9.3&#8722;12.7) in the placebo arm (HR, 0.78; 95% CI, 0.63&#8722;0.97; <em>

5648P</em>

5649 = .0249).</li>

5650<li>

5651An IRC assessment of the triplet therapy found a PFS of 16 months (95% CI, 11.3&#8722;18.5) compared with 12 months in the control arm (95% CI, 10.8&#8722;14.7) (HR, 0.85; 95% CI, 0.67&#8722;1.07).</li>

5652<li>

5653Objective response rates and CRs were similar between the treatment groups.</li>

5654<li>

5655Data are not mature for OS.</li>

5656<li>

5657 Serious AEs and treatment discontinuations because of toxicity were similar between the arms. Grade 5 AEs occurred in seven patients in each arm. Two patients with hepatic failure in the atezolizumab group and one patient with pulmonary hemorrhage in the control group were considered treatment related.</li>

5658</ul>

5659</div>

5660</li>

5661</ol>

5662</div>

5663<p id="_1304" tabindex="-1">

5664The impact of triplet therapy on OS, or when compared with checkpoint inhibitor monotherapy, or to sequential therapy with combination BRAF-MEK inhibitor therapy, preceded or followed by checkpoint inhibition (ongoing trial <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02224781">

5665NCT02224781</a>

5666) is unknown.</p>

5667</section>

5668</section>

5669</section>

5670<section id="_841">

5671<h4 id="_841_toc">

5672Chemotherapy</h4>

5673<p id="_842" tabindex="-1">

5674Dacarbazine was approved in 1970 on the basis of objective response rates. Phase III trials indicate an objective response rate of 10% to 20%, with rare CRs observed. An impact on OS has not been demonstrated in randomized trials.[<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

56757</a>

5676,<a href="#cit/section_9.20">

567720</a>

5678,<a href="#cit/section_9.35">

567935</a>

5680-<a href="#cit/section_9.37">

568137</a>

5682] When used as a control arm for recent registration trials of ipilimumab and vemurafenib in previously untreated patients with metastatic melanoma, dacarbazine was inferior for OS.</p>

5683<p id="_843" tabindex="-1">

5684Temozolomide, an oral alkylating agent that hydrolyzes to the same active moiety as dacarbazine, appeared to be similar to dacarbazine (IV administration) in a randomized, phase III trial with a primary end point of OS. However, the trial was designed for superiority, and the sample size was inadequate to prove equivalency.[<a href="#cit/section_9.36">

568536</a>

5686]</p>

5687<p id="_844" tabindex="-1">

5688The objective response rate to dacarbazine and the nitrosoureas, carmustine and lomustine, is approximately 10% to 20%.[<a href="#cit/section_9.35">

568935</a>

5690,<a href="#cit/section_9.38">

569138</a>

5692-<a href="#cit/section_9.40">

569340</a>

5694] Responses are usually short-lived, ranging from 3 to 6 months, although long-term remissions can occur in a limited number of patients who attain a CR.[<a href="#cit/section_9.38">

569538</a>

5696,<a href="#cit/section_9.40">

569740</a>

5698]</p>

5699<p id="_845" tabindex="-1">

5700A randomized trial compared IV dacarbazine with temozolomide, an oral agent; OS was 6.4 months for dacarbazine versus 7.7 months for temozolomide (HR, 1.18; 95% CI, 0.92&#8211;1.52). While these data suggested similarity between dacarbazine and temozolomide, no benefit in survival has been demonstrated for either dacarbazine or temozolomide; therefore, demonstration of similarity did not result in FDA approval of temozolomide.[<a href="#cit/section_9.36">

570136</a>

5702][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5703Level of evidence A1</a>

5704]</p>

5705<p id="_846" tabindex="-1">

5706An extended schedule and escalated dose of temozolomide was compared with dacarbazine in a multicenter trial by the European Organisation for Research and Treatment of Cancer (EORTC) (EORTC-18032 [NCT00101218]) randomly assigning 859 patients. No improvement was seen in OS or PFS for the temozolomide group, and this dose and schedule resulted in more toxicity than standard-dose, single-agent dacarbazine.[<a href="#cit/section_9.41">

570741</a>

5708][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5709Level of evidence A1</a>

5710] </p>

5711<p id="_847" tabindex="-1">

5712Two randomized phase III trials in previously untreated patients with metastatic melanoma (resulting in FDA approval for vemurafenib [<a href="#cit/section_9.20">

571320</a>

5714] and ipilimumab [<a href="#cit/section_9.7">

57157</a>

5716]) included dacarbazine as the standard therapy arm. Both vemurafenib (in <em class="gene-name">

5717BRAF</em>

5718 V600 mutant melanoma) and ipilimumab showed superior OS compared with dacarbazine in the two separate trials.</p>

5719<p id="_848" tabindex="-1">

5720Other agents with modest, single-agent activity include vinca alkaloids, platinum compounds, and taxanes.[<a href="#cit/section_9.38">

572138</a>

5722,<a href="#cit/section_9.39">

572339</a>

5724]</p>

5725<p id="_849" tabindex="-1">

5726Attempts to develop combination regimens that incorporate chemotherapy (e.g., multiagent chemotherapy,[<a href="#cit/section_9.42">

572742</a>

5728,<a href="#cit/section_9.43">

572943</a>

5730] combinations of chemotherapy and tamoxifen,[<a href="#cit/section_9.44">

573144</a>

5732-<a href="#cit/section_9.46">

573346</a>

5734] and combinations of chemotherapy and immunotherapy [<a href="#cit/section_9.10">

573510</a>

5736,<a href="#cit/section_9.11">

573711</a>

5738,<a href="#cit/section_9.42">

573942</a>

5740,<a href="#cit/section_9.47">

574147</a>

5742-<a href="#cit/section_9.50">

574350</a>

5744]) have not demonstrated an improvement in OS. </p>

5745<p id="_850" tabindex="-1">

5746A published data meta-analysis of 18 randomized trials (15 of which had survival information) that compared chemotherapy with biochemotherapy (i.e., the same chemotherapy plus interferon alone or with IL-2) reported no impact on OS.[<a href="#cit/section_9.51">

574751</a>

5748][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5749Level of evidence A1</a>

5750] </p>

5751</section>

5752<section id="_851">

5753<h4 id="_851_toc">

5754Palliative local therapy</h4>

5755<p id="_852" tabindex="-1">

5756Melanoma metastatic to distant, lymph node&#8211;bearing areas may be palliated by regional lymphadenectomy. Isolated metastases to the lung, gastrointestinal tract, bone, or sometimes the brain may be palliated by resection, with occasional long-term survival.[<a href="#cit/section_9.48">

575748</a>

5758-<a href="#cit/section_9.50">

575950</a>

5760]</p>

5761<p id="_853" tabindex="-1">

5762Although melanoma is a relatively radiation-resistant tumor, palliative radiation therapy may alleviate symptoms. Retrospective studies have shown that symptom relief and some shrinkage of the tumor with radiation therapy may occur in patients with the following:[<a href="#cit/section_9.52">

576352</a>

5764,<a href="#cit/section_9.53">

576553</a>

5766]</p>

5767<div class="pdq-content-list">

5768<ul id="_854">

5769<li>

5770 Multiple brain metastases. </li>

5771<li>

5772 Bone metastases. </li>

5773<li>

5774 Spinal cord compression.</li>

5775</ul>

5776</div>

5777<p id="_855" tabindex="-1">

5778The most effective dose-fractionation schedule for palliation of melanoma metastatic to the bone or spinal cord is unclear, but high-dose-per-fraction schedules are sometimes used to overcome tumor resistance. For more information, see <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/pain/pain-hp-pdq">

5779Cancer Pain</a>

5780.</p>

5781</section>

5782</section>

5783<section id="_177">

5784<h3 id="_177_toc">
