5785Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation for Unresectable Stage III, Stage IV, and Recurrent Melanoma</h3>

5786<div class="pdq-content-list">

5787<ol id="_474">

5788<li>

5789Immunotherapy&#8212;single agent and combination immunomodulation.</li>

5790<li>

5791Targeted therapy&#8212;single-agent and combination therapy.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5792<ol id="_806" class="lower-alpha">

5793<li>

5794Signal transduction inhibitors, including PI3K (phosphoinositide-3 kinase) and Akt (protein kinase B) inhibitors, CDK (cyclin-dependent kinase) in addition to BRAF and MEK inhibitors.</li>

5795<li>

5796Antiangiogenesis agents. Preclinical data suggest that increased vascular endothelial growth factor production may be implicated in resistance to BRAF inhibitors.[<a href="#cit/section_9.54">

579754</a>

5798]</li>

5799<li>

5800Targeted therapy for specific melanoma populations.<div class="pdq-content-list">

5801<ul id="_799">

5802<li>

5803 In smaller subsets of melanoma, activating mutations may occur in <em class="gene-name">

5804NRAS</em>

5805 (15%&#8211;20%), <em class="gene-name">

5806c-KIT</em>

5807 (28%&#8211;39% of melanomas arising in chronically sun-damaged skin, or acral and mucosal melanomas), and <em class="gene-name">

5808CDK4</em>

5809 (&lt;5%), whereas <em class="gene-name">

5810GNAQ</em>

5811 is frequently mutated in uveal melanomas. Drugs developed to target the pathways activated by these mutations are currently in clinical trials.</li>

5812</ul>

5813</div>

5814</li>

5815</ol>

5816</div>

5817</li>

5818<li>

5819Combinations of immunotherapy and targeted therapy.</li>

5820<li>

5821 Intralesional injections (for example, oncolytic viruses).</li>

5822<li>

5823Complete surgical resection of all known disease versus best medical therapy.</li>

5824<li>

5825Isolated limb perfusion for unresectable extremity melanoma.</li>

5826<li>

5827Systemic therapy for unresectable disease.</li>

5828</ol>

5829</div>

5830</section>

5833Current Clinical Trials</h3>

5835Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

5836advanced clinical trial search</a>

5837 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

5838General information</a>

5839 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

6067 <section id="_216">

6068

6069 <h2>

6070Changes to This Summary (01/31/2023)</h2>

6071

6072 <div id="_section_216" class="pdq-sections">

6073<p id="_217" tabindex="-1">

6074The PDQ cancer information summaries are reviewed regularly and updated as new information becomes available. This section describes the latest changes made to this summary as of the date above.</p>

6075<p id="_1333" tabindex="-1">

6076<strong>

6077<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_1">

6078General Information About Melanoma</a>

6079</strong>

6080</p>

6081<p id="_1334" tabindex="-1">

6082Updated <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_6">

6083statistics</a>

6084 with estimated new cases and deaths for 2023 (cited American Cancer Society as reference 1). </p>

6085<p id="_1335" tabindex="-1">

6086Revised <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_750">

6087text</a>

6088 to state that since the early 2000s, the incidence of melanoma in people younger than 50 years declined by about 1% per year in men and stabilized in women. From 2015 to 2019, the incidence in people aged 50 years and older stabilized in men and increased by about 1% per year in women.</p>

6089<p id="_disclaimerHP_3" tabindex="-1">

6090This summary is written and maintained by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

6091PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

6092, which is

6093editorially independent of NCI. The summary reflects an independent review of

6094the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or NIH. More

6095information about summary policies and the role of the PDQ Editorial Boards in

6096maintaining the PDQ summaries can be found on the <a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq#_AboutThis_1">

6097About This PDQ Summary</a>

6098 and <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq">

6099PDQ&#174; Cancer Information for Health Professionals</a>

6100 pages.

6101</p>

6102</div>

6110 <h2>

6111About This PDQ Summary</h2>

6112

6113 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

6114<section id="_AboutThis_2">

6115<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

6116Purpose of This Summary</h3>

6117<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

6118This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of melanoma. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

6119</section>

6120<section id="_AboutThis_4">

6121<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

6122Reviewers and Updates</h3>

6123<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

6124This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

6125PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

6126, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

6127<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

6128 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

6129<div class="pdq-content-list">

6130<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

6131<li>

6132be discussed at a meeting,</li>

6133<li>

6134be cited with text, or</li>

6135<li>

6136replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

6137</ul>

6138</div>

6139<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

6140Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

6141<p id="" tabindex="-1">

6142The lead reviewers for Melanoma Treatment are:</p>

6143<div class="pdq-content-list">

6144<ul id="">

6145<li>

6146Russell S. Berman, MD (New York University School of Medicine)</li>

6147<li>

6148Shaheer A. Khan, PhD (Columbia University Irving Medical Center)</li>

6149</ul>

6150</div>

6151<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

6152Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

6153Email Us</a>

6154. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

6155</section>

6156<section id="_AboutThis_10">

6157<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

6158Levels of Evidence</h3>

6159<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

6160Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

6161formal evidence ranking system</a>

6162 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

6163</section>

6164<section id="_AboutThis_12">

6165<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

6166Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

6167<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

6168PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

6169<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

6170The preferred citation for this PDQ summary is:</p>

6171<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

6172PDQ&#174; Adult Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Melanoma Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq">

6173https://www.cancer.gov/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq</a>

6174. Accessed &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. [PMID: 26389469]</p>

6175<p id="_AboutThis_16" tabindex="-1">

6176Images in this summary are used with permission of the author(s), artist, and/or publisher for use within the PDQ summaries only. Permission to use images outside the context of PDQ information must be obtained from the owner(s) and cannot be granted by the National Cancer Institute. Information about using the illustrations in this summary, along with many other cancer-related images, is available in <a href="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/" title="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/">

6177Visuals Online</a>

6178, a collection of over 2,000 scientific images.

6179

6180</p>

6181</section>

6182<section id="_AboutThis_17">

6183<h3 id="_AboutThis_17_toc">

6184Disclaimer</h3>

6185<p id="_AboutThis_18" tabindex="-1">

6186Based on the strength of the available evidence, treatment options may be described as either &#8220;standard&#8221; or &#8220;under clinical evaluation.&#8221; These classifications should not be used as a basis for insurance reimbursement determinations. More information on insurance coverage is available on Cancer.gov on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care">

6187Managing Cancer Care</a>

6188 page.</p>

6189</section>

6198.</p>
